# 21
```
**1. abject**
1. **Definition:** (of a situation or condition) extremely bad, unpleasant, and degrading.
2. **Concise Meaning:** extremely bad and degrading
3. **Sentences:**
    * The family lived in **abject** poverty after losing their home.
    * His apology was **abject**, filled with shame and remorse.
4. **Opposite Words:** noble, commendable
5. **GRE Synonyms:** despicable, ignoble

**2. amicable**
1. **Definition:** (of relations between people) having a spirit of friendliness; without serious disagreement or rancour.
2. **Concise Meaning:** friendly and agreeable relations
3. **Sentences:**
    * They reached an **amicable** settlement in their divorce.
    * The meeting ended on an **amicable** note.
4. **Opposite Words:** hostile, unfriendly
5. **GRE Synonyms:** cordial, convivial

**3. animosity**
1. **Definition:** strong hostility.
2. **Concise Meaning:** strong hostility or dislike
3. **Sentences:**
    * There was deep **animosity** between the rival gangs.
    * Her **animosity** towards him was clearly visible.
4. **Opposite Words:** goodwill, friendliness
5. **GRE Synonyms:** antipathy, enmity

**4. aver**
1. **Definition:** state or assert to be the case.
2. **Concise Meaning:** assert or declare confidently
3. **Sentences:**
    * He **averred** his innocence in court.
    * The witness **averred** seeing the incident clearly.
4. **Opposite Words:** deny, contradict
5. **GRE Synonyms:** affirm, avouch

**5. barrage(1)**
1. **Definition:** a concentrated artillery bombardment over an area.
2. **Concise Meaning:** concentrated artillery bombardment
3. **Sentences:**
    * The troops advanced under a heavy artillery **barrage**.
    * The enemy launched a relentless **barrage** of fire.
4. **Opposite Words:** lull, silence
5. **GRE Synonyms:** cannonade, bombardment

**6. barrage(2)**
1. **Definition:** a concentrated or overwhelming outpouring of something.
2. **Concise Meaning:** overwhelming outpouring of something
3. **Sentences:**
    * She faced a **barrage** of questions from reporters.
    * He was met with a **barrage** of criticism online.
4. **Opposite Words:** trickle, dearth
5. **GRE Synonyms:** deluge, torrent

**7. cathartic**
1. **Definition:** providing psychological relief through the open expression of strong emotions; causing catharsis.
2. **Concise Meaning:** emotionally releasing, purifying
3. **Sentences:**
    * Crying can be a **cathartic** experience after loss.
    * Screaming was a **cathartic** release of frustration.
4. **Opposite Words:** suppressing, bottling up
5. **GRE Synonyms:** purgative, cleansing

**8. decipher**
1. **Definition:** succeed in understanding, interpreting, or identifying (something).
2. **Concise Meaning:** decode or interpret meaning
3. **Sentences:**
    * I struggled to **decipher** his messy handwriting.
    * Experts try to **decipher** ancient scripts.
4. **Opposite Words:** obscure, confuse
5. **GRE Synonyms:** construe, decode

**9. delusion**
1. **Definition:** an idiosyncratic belief or impression that is firmly maintained despite being contradicted by what is generally accepted as reality or rational argument, typically a symptom of mental disorder.
2. **Concise Meaning:** false belief or impression
3. **Sentences:**
    * He lived under the **delusion** he was still young.
    * Her belief in magic was a harmless **delusion**.
4. **Opposite Words:** reality, truth
5. **GRE Synonyms:** hallucination, illusion

**10. dispense(1)**
1. **Definition:** distribute or provide (a service or information) to a number of people.
2. **Concise Meaning:** distribute or provide service
3. **Sentences:**
    * The nurse **dispensed** medication to patients.
    * The charity **dispenses** aid to the needy.
4. **Opposite Words:** withhold, keep
5. **GRE Synonyms:** administer, allocate

**11. dispense(2)**
1. **Definition:** manage without or get rid of.
2. **Concise Meaning:** manage without, get rid of
3. **Sentences:**
    * We can **dispense** with formalities now.
    * They decided to **dispense** with old furniture.
4. **Opposite Words:** retain, keep
5. **GRE Synonyms:** discard, forgo

**12. eloquent**
1. **Definition:** fluent or persuasive speaking or writing.
2. **Concise Meaning:** fluent and persuasive speaking
3. **Sentences:**
    * She gave an **eloquent** speech on climate change.
    * His writing is **eloquent** and deeply moving.
4. **Opposite Words:** inarticulate, hesitant
5. **GRE Synonyms:** articulate, expressive

**13. enthrall**
1. **Definition:** capture the fascinated attention of.
2. **Concise Meaning:** fascinate or captivate attention
3. **Sentences:**
    * The story of adventure **enthralled** us all.
    * The magician's tricks **enthralled** the audience.
4. **Opposite Words:** bore, disenchant
5. **GRE Synonyms:** captivate, mesmerize

**14. eradicate**
1. **Definition:** destroy completely; put an end to.
2. **Concise Meaning:** destroy completely, eliminate
3. **Sentences:**
    * Vaccination aims to **eradicate** deadly diseases.
    * We must **eradicate** poverty from our society.
4. **Opposite Words:** create, establish
5. **GRE Synonyms:** annihilate, extirpate

**15. fledgling(1)**
1. **Definition:** a young bird that has just fledged or become capable of flying.
2. **Concise Meaning:** young bird leaving nest
3. **Sentences:**
    * The **fledgling** robin hopped in the garden.
    * We watched the **fledgling** take its first flight.
4. **Opposite Words:** mature bird, adult bird
5. **GRE Synonyms:** nestling, hatchling

**16. fledgling(2)**
1. **Definition:** a person or organization that is immature, inexperienced, or underdeveloped.
2. **Concise Meaning:** new and inexperienced person
3. **Sentences:**
    * The company is still a **fledgling** in tech.
    * He is a **fledgling** writer starting his career.
4. **Opposite Words:** experienced, veteran
5. **GRE Synonyms:** novice, tyro

**17. fortitude**
1. **Definition:** courage in pain or adversity.
2. **Concise Meaning:** courage in adversity
3. **Sentences:**
    * She showed great **fortitude** during her illness.
    * He faced challenges with remarkable **fortitude**.
4. **Opposite Words:** cowardice, weakness
5. **GRE Synonyms:** resilience, grit

**18. fortuitous**
1. **Definition:** happening by chance or accident rather than design.
2. **Concise Meaning:** happening by lucky chance
3. **Sentences:**
    * Meeting her was a **fortuitous** event.
    * The discovery was a **fortuitous** accident.
4. **Opposite Words:** planned, deliberate
5. **GRE Synonyms:** serendipitous, adventitious

**19. goad**
1. **Definition:** provoke or annoy (someone) so as to stimulate some action or reaction.
2. **Concise Meaning:** provoke to stimulate action
3. **Sentences:**
    * He was **goaded** into fighting by friends.
    * The coach **goaded** the team to perform better.
4. **Opposite Words:** deter, dissuade
5. **GRE Synonyms:** incite, spur

**20. imminent**
1. **Definition:** about to happen.
2. **Concise Meaning:** about to happen soon
3. **Sentences:**
    * Rain is **imminent**, look at those clouds.
    * Danger of war is **imminent** in the region.
4. **Opposite Words:** distant, remote
5. **GRE Synonyms:** impending, proximate

**21. incontrovertible**
1. **Definition:** not able to be denied or disputed.
2. **Concise Meaning:** undeniable, not disputable
3. **Sentences:**
    * The evidence presented was **incontrovertible**.
    * It is an **incontrovertible** scientific fact.
4. **Opposite Words:** disputable, questionable
5. **GRE Synonyms:** indubitable, unassailable

**22. itinerant**
1. **Definition:** travelling from place to place.
2. **Concise Meaning:** traveling from place to place
3. **Sentences:**
    * The **itinerant** musician traveled the country.
    * He lived an **itinerant** life as a salesman.
4. **Opposite Words:** settled, stationary
5. **GRE Synonyms:** nomadic, peripatetic

**23. magnanimous**
1. **Definition:** very generous or forgiving, especially towards a rival or someone less powerful than oneself.
2. **Concise Meaning:** generous and forgiving spirit
3. **Sentences:**
    * He was **magnanimous** in victory.
    * She showed a **magnanimous** forgiving nature.
4. **Opposite Words:** petty, selfish
5. **GRE Synonyms:** benevolent, munificent

**24. meritorious**
1. **Definition:** deserving reward or praise.
2. **Concise Meaning:** deserving praise or reward
3. **Sentences:**
    * His actions were deemed **meritorious**.
    * She received award for **meritorious** service.
4. **Opposite Words:** unworthy, despicable
5. **GRE Synonyms:** laudable, estimable

**25. mutiny**
1. **Definition:** an open rebellion against the proper authorities, especially by soldiers or sailors against their officers.
2. **Concise Meaning:** rebellion against authority
3. **Sentences:**
    * The sailors staged a **mutiny** at sea.
    * The **mutiny** was suppressed by loyal forces.
4. **Opposite Words:** obedience, loyalty
5. **GRE Synonyms:** insurrection, revolt

**26. paradoxical**
1. **Definition:** seemingly absurd or self-contradictory.
2. **Concise Meaning:** self-contradictory, absurd
3. **Sentences:**
    * Poverty in wealth is quite **paradoxical**.
    * "Less is more" is a **paradoxical** statement.
4. **Opposite Words:** consistent, logical
5. **GRE Synonyms:** anomalous, incongruous

**27. perseverance**
1. **Definition:** persistence in doing something despite difficulty or delay in achieving success.
2. **Concise Meaning:** persistence despite difficulty
3. **Sentences:**
    * **Perseverance** is key to long term success.
    * Her **perseverance** led to marathon finish.
4. **Opposite Words:** apathy, indolence
5. **GRE Synonyms:** tenacity, assiduity

**28. render(1)**
1. **Definition:** provide or give (a service, help, etc.).
2. **Concise Meaning:** provide or give service
3. **Sentences:**
    * They **rendered** assistance to flood victims.
    * The company **renders** financial services.
4. **Opposite Words:** withhold, deprive
5. **GRE Synonyms:** furnish, impart

**29. render(2)**
1. **Definition:** cause to be or become; make.
2. **Concise Meaning:** cause to become, make
3. **Sentences:**
    * The heat **rendered** him weak and faint.
    * The music **rendered** her speechless with awe.
4. **Opposite Words:** undo, destroy
5. **GRE Synonyms:** make, cause

**30. repertoire(1)**
1. **Definition:** a stock of plays, dances, or items that a company or a performer knows or is prepared to perform.
2. **Concise Meaning:** performance pieces, stock
3. **Sentences:**
    * The ballet company has a vast **repertoire**.
    * This song is part of band's usual **repertoire**.
4. **Opposite Words:** N/A
5. **GRE Synonyms:** collection, stock

**31. repertoire(2)**
1. **Definition:** the whole quantity of items or skills of a particular kind.
2. **Concise Meaning:** range of skills or items
3. **Sentences:**
    * Cooking is in her **repertoire** of skills.
    * The chef expanded his culinary **repertoire**.
4. **Opposite Words:** limitation, lack
5. **GRE Synonyms:** range, inventory

**32. resilient(1)**
1. **Definition:** (of a person or animal) able to withstand or recover quickly from difficult conditions.
2. **Concise Meaning:** recover quickly from difficulty
3. **Sentences:**
    * Children are often very **resilient** people.
    * The economy is proving quite **resilient**.
4. **Opposite Words:** fragile, weak
5. **GRE Synonyms:** robust, hardy

**33. resilient(2)**
1. **Definition:** (of a material or object) able to recoil or spring back into shape after bending, stretching, or being compressed.
2. **Concise Meaning:** spring back into shape
3. **Sentences:**
    * Rubber is a highly **resilient** material.
    * The **resilient** fabric regained its shape.
4. **Opposite Words:** inflexible, rigid
5. **GRE Synonyms:** elastic, springy

**34. resolute**
1. **Definition:** admirably purposeful, determined, and unwavering.
2. **Concise Meaning:** determined and unwavering
3. **Sentences:**
    * She was **resolute** in her decision to quit.
    * He remained **resolute** despite many obstacles.
4. **Opposite Words:** irresolute, wavering
5. **GRE Synonyms:** steadfast, tenacious

**35. supple**
1. **Definition:** bending and moving easily and gracefully; flexible.
2. **Concise Meaning:** flexible and graceful movement
3. **Sentences:**
    * Yoga helps keep your body **supple**.
    * The leather is **supple** and very soft.
4. **Opposite Words:** stiff, rigid
5. **GRE Synonyms:** lithe, pliable

**36. valor**
1. **Definition:** great courage in the face of danger, especially in battle.
2. **Concise Meaning:** courage in danger or battle
3. **Sentences:**
    * He received medal for his battlefield **valor**.
    * Soldiers fought with extraordinary **valor**.
4. **Opposite Words:** cowardice, fear
5. **GRE Synonyms:** bravery, heroism
```

# 22
**1. arresting**
1. **Definition:** Striking; eye-catching; attracting attention; impressive.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Strikingly impressive and attention-grabbing
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her **arresting** beauty made everyone in the room turn to look.
    *  The painting's **arresting** use of color immediately drew the viewer in.
4. **Opposite Words:**  unremarkable, ordinary
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  captivating, striking

**2. chastise**
1. **Definition:** Rebuke or reprimand severely.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To severely reprimand or scold
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The teacher **chastised** the students for their disruptive behavior.
    *  He was publicly **chastised** for his unethical actions.
4. **Opposite Words:**  praise, commend
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  reproach, castigate

**3. cumbersome**
1. **Definition:** Large or heavy and therefore difficult to carry or use; slow or complicated and therefore inefficient.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Heavy, awkward, and inefficient
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The old filing system was incredibly **cumbersome** and time-consuming.
    *  Carrying the **cumbersome** package up the stairs was a struggle.
4. **Opposite Words:**  manageable, convenient
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  unwieldy, ponderous

**4. economy**
1. **Definition:** The state of a country or region in terms of the production and consumption of goods and services; thrifty and efficient use of material resources or effort.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Careful use of resources; thriftiness
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She practiced **economy** by always turning off the lights when leaving a room.
    *  The design of the car focused on fuel **economy** and efficiency.
4. **Opposite Words:**  wastefulness, extravagance
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  frugality, parsimony

**5. elementary**
1. **Definition:** Relating to the basic facts of a subject; simple and not advanced.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Basic, fundamental, and simple
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The instructions were **elementary** and easy to follow.
    *  **Elementary** math skills are essential for everyday life.
4. **Opposite Words:**  advanced, complex
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  rudimentary, fundamental

**6. embellish(1)**
1. **Definition:** Make (something) more attractive by the addition of decorative details or features.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Add details to make attractive
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She **embellished** her dress with lace and ribbons for the party.
    *  He decided to **embellish** the story with fictional details.
4. **Opposite Words:**  simplify, strip
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  adorn, decorate

**7. embellish(2)**
1. **Definition:** Make (a statement or story) more interesting or entertaining by adding extra details, especially ones that are not true.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Exaggerate a story or statement
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He tended to **embellish** his stories to make himself seem more important.
    *  Don't **embellish** the truth; just tell me what really happened.
4. **Opposite Words:**  understate, simplify
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  exaggerate, overstate

**8. euphoric**
1. **Definition:** Characterized by or feeling intense excitement and happiness.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Feeling intensely happy and excited
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She felt **euphoric** after winning the competition.
    *  The crowd was **euphoric** after the team scored the winning goal.
4. **Opposite Words:**  depressed, despondent
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  ecstatic, elated

**9. exonerate**
1. **Definition:** Absolve (someone) from blame for a fault or wrongdoing, especially after due consideration of the case.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Clear from blame or guilt
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The new evidence **exonerated** him from the crime.
    *  She was finally **exonerated** after years of wrongful accusations.
4. **Opposite Words:**  convict, incriminate
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  vindicate, acquit

**10. extrapolate**
1. **Definition:** Extend the application of (a method or conclusion, especially one based on statistics) to an unknown situation by assuming that existing trends will continue or similar methods will be applicable.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Infer from known data; predict
3. **Sentences:**
    *  We can **extrapolate** future trends from the current data.
    *  Scientists **extrapolate** climate change effects based on current observations.
4. **Opposite Words:**  interpolate, deduce
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  infer, deduce

**11. falter**
1. **Definition:** Start to lose strength or momentum; speak hesitantly or unsteadily.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Hesitate or lose momentum
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her voice began to **falter** as she recounted the tragic story.
    *  The economy began to **falter** after the initial boom.
4. **Opposite Words:**  persist, stabilize
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  waver, hesitate

**12. fervent**
1. **Definition:** Having or displaying a passionate intensity.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Passionate and intensely enthusiastic
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He is a **fervent** supporter of animal rights.
    *  Her **fervent** belief in justice motivated her activism.
4. **Opposite Words:**  apathetic, indifferent
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  ardent, zealous

**13. foment**
1. **Definition:** Instigate or stir up (an undesirable or violent sentiment or course of action).
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Stir up negative feelings; incite
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The politician was accused of **fomenting** unrest among the people.
    *  Rumors can **foment** distrust and suspicion within a community.
4. **Opposite Words:**  suppress, quell
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  incite, instigate

**14. gaffe**
1. **Definition:** An unintentional act or remark causing embarrassment to its originator or audience; a blunder.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Social blunder; embarrassing mistake
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He realized he had made a terrible **gaffe** when he insulted his boss's wife.
    *  Her awkward silence after the **gaffe** made the situation even worse.
4. **Opposite Words:**  tact, diplomacy
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  blunder, faux pas

**15. heterodox**
1. **Definition:** Not conforming with accepted or orthodox standards or beliefs.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Unorthodox, unconventional, nonconformist
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **heterodox** views on education were considered radical.
    *  The artist's **heterodox** style challenged traditional art conventions.
4. **Opposite Words:**  orthodox, conventional
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  unconventional, unorthodox

**16. histrionic**
1. **Definition:** Excessively theatrical or dramatic in character or style.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Overly dramatic or theatrical
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her **histrionic** reaction to the minor inconvenience was unnecessary.
    *  He delivered a **histrionic** speech filled with exaggerated emotions.
4. **Opposite Words:**  understated, subdued
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  melodramatic, theatrical

**17. implicit**
1. **Definition:** Implied though not plainly expressed.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Implied but not directly stated
3. **Sentences:**
    *  There was an **implicit** agreement between them to keep the secret.
    *  Her silence was an **implicit** refusal to cooperate.
4. **Opposite Words:**  explicit, stated
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  tacit, implied

**18. inviolate**
1. **Definition:** Free or safe from injury or violation.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Pure, untouched, free from violation
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The sacred temple was considered **inviolate** ground.
    *  He vowed to keep his promise **inviolate**.
4. **Opposite Words:**  violated, profaned
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  sacrosanct, unprofaned

**19. liability**
1. **Definition:** The state of being responsible for something, especially by law; a person or thing whose presence or behavior is likely to cause embarrassment or put one at a disadvantage.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Legal responsibility; disadvantageous thing
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The company accepted **liability** for the accident.
    *  His impulsive behavior was becoming a **liability** to the team.
4. **Opposite Words:**  asset, advantage
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  burden, impediment

**20. obstinate**
1. **Definition:** Stubbornly refusing to change one's opinion or chosen course of action, despite attempts to persuade one to do so.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Stubbornly refusing to change mind
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He was too **obstinate** to admit that he was wrong.
    *  Her **obstinate** refusal to listen to advice led to problems.
4. **Opposite Words:**  compliant, yielding
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  intransigent, obdurate

**21. painstaking**
1. **Definition:** Done with or employing great care and thoroughness.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Very careful and thorough
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The artist created the sculpture with **painstaking** detail.
    *  The investigation was a **painstaking** process that took months.
4. **Opposite Words:**  careless, negligent
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  meticulous, assiduous

**22. phlegmatic**
1. **Definition:** Having an unemotional and stolidly calm disposition.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Calm, unemotional, and stoic
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Despite the chaos around him, he remained remarkably **phlegmatic**.
    *  Her **phlegmatic** nature made her an excellent negotiator.
4. **Opposite Words:**  excitable, emotional
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  impassive, apathetic

**23. prodigious**
1. **Definition:** Remarkably or impressively great in extent, size, or degree.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Remarkably large, impressive, extraordinary
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The athlete displayed **prodigious** strength and speed.
    *  She had a **prodigious** talent for music, mastering multiple instruments.
4. **Opposite Words:**  small, insignificant
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  immense, colossal

**24. propensity**
1. **Definition:** An inclination or natural tendency to behave in a particular way.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Natural inclination or tendency
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He has a **propensity** for making impulsive decisions.
    *  Her **propensity** for kindness made her well-loved.
4. **Opposite Words:**  aversion, disinclination
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  predilection, proclivity

**25. qualm**
1. **Definition:** A feeling of unease or doubt, especially about one's own conduct; a misgiving.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Feeling of doubt or unease
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He had no **qualms** about lying to protect his friend.
    *  She felt a **qualm** of guilt after taking the last piece of cake.
4. **Opposite Words:**  certainty, confidence
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  scruple, misgiving

**26. renege**
1. **Definition:** Go back on a promise, undertaking, or contract.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Break a promise or agreement
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He **reneged** on his promise to help her move.
    *  The company **reneged** on the contract after the market changed.
4. **Opposite Words:**  honor, uphold
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  default, retract

**27. stint**
1. **Definition:** Supply an ungenerous or inadequate amount of (something).
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Restrict or limit in amount
3. **Sentences:**
    *  They did not **stint** on the decorations for the party.
    *  The company **stinted** on employee benefits to cut costs.
4. **Opposite Words:**  lavish, squander
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  economize, restrict

**28. temper**
1. **Definition:** Improve the temperamental qualities of (something, especially steel) by heat treatment; moderate (something) in particular qualities.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Moderate or soften something
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He tried to **temper** his criticism with constructive suggestions.
    *  The artist **tempered** the harsh colors with softer hues.
4. **Opposite Words:**  intensify, aggravate
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  moderate, mitigate

**29. tentative**
1. **Definition:** Not certain or fixed; provisional.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Uncertain, hesitant, provisional
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The plans are still **tentative** and subject to change.
    *  She offered a **tentative** smile, unsure of his reaction.
4. **Opposite Words:**  definite, certain
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  provisional, hesitant

**30. unprecedented**
1. **Definition:** Never done or known before.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Never happened or known before
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The storm caused **unprecedented** damage to the coastline.
    *  The company's growth was **unprecedented** in the industry.
4. **Opposite Words:**  common, usual
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  novel, unparalleled

**31. vivacious**
1. **Definition:** Attractively lively and animated.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Lively, animated, and energetic
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her **vivacious** personality made her the life of the party.
    *  The dancer was known for her **vivacious** and energetic performances.
4. **Opposite Words:**  lethargic, dull
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  ebullient, animated

# 23
**1. allusive**
1. **Definition:** Working by suggestion rather than explicit mention.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Indirectly hinting at something
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her writing style is **allusive**, often referencing classical myths.
    *  The comedian's **allusive** jokes required some background knowledge.
4. **Opposite Words:** explicit, direct
5. **GRE Synonyms:** suggestive, referential

**2. astute**
1. **Definition:** Having or showing an ability to accurately assess situations or people and turn this to one's advantage.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Clever and perceptive; shrewd
3. **Sentences:**
    *  An **astute** businessman quickly saw the market opportunity.
    *  She made an **astute** observation about the political climate.
4. **Opposite Words:** naive, foolish
5. **GRE Synonyms:** shrewd, perspicacious

**3. commence**
1. **Definition:** Begin; start.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To begin or to start
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The graduation ceremony will **commence** at 10 AM.
    *  Construction on the new building is set to **commence** next month.
4. **Opposite Words:** conclude, finish
5. **GRE Synonyms:** initiate, inaugurate

**4. convalescent**
1. **Definition:** (of a person) recovering from an illness or operation.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Recovering from sickness or injury
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He is currently **convalescent** after his surgery.
    *  The **convalescent** patient was regaining strength slowly.
4. **Opposite Words:** declining, worsening
5. **GRE Synonyms:** recuperating, mending

**5. curb**
1. **Definition:** Control or restrain.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To restrain or control something
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The government should **curb** excessive spending.
    *  He needs to **curb** his impulsive behavior.
4. **Opposite Words:** encourage, incite
5. **GRE Synonyms:** restrain, suppress

**6. decry**
1. **Definition:** Publicly denounce.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Publicly criticize or condemn
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Activists **decry** the corporation's environmental policies.
    *  Many people **decry** the violence in the film.
4. **Opposite Words:** praise, commend
5. **GRE Synonyms:** denounce, condemn

**7. duress**
1. **Definition:** Compulsion by threat or force; coercion.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Force or threats; coercion
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He confessed under **duress** and later recanted his statement.
    *  The contract was signed under **duress**, making it invalid.
4. **Opposite Words:** free will, volition
5. **GRE Synonyms:** coercion, compulsion

**8. evoke**
1. **Definition:** Bring or recall (a feeling, memory, or image) to the conscious mind.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To summon or bring forth
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The old photograph **evoked** memories of childhood summers.
    *  The music **evoked** a feeling of nostalgia.
4. **Opposite Words:** suppress, quell
5. **GRE Synonyms:** elicit, conjure

**9. fawn**
1. **Definition:** Give a servile display of exaggerated flattery and affection, typically in order to gain favour or advantage.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To flatter excessively; be servile
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The employees **fawn** over the manager to get promotions.
    *  He **fawned** on the celebrity hoping for an autograph.
4. **Opposite Words:** scorn, disregard
5. **GRE Synonyms:** grovel, kowtow

**10. fret**
1. **Definition:** Be constantly or visibly worried or anxious.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To worry excessively or anxiously
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Don't **fret** about the small details; focus on the big picture.
    *  She tends to **fret** over things she cannot control.
4. **Opposite Words:** relax, reassure
5. **GRE Synonyms:** worry, agonize

**11. glib**
1. **Definition:** (of words or people) fluent and voluble but insincere and shallow.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Fluent, insincere, and shallow
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **glib** answers failed to address the serious concerns.
    *  The politician's **glib** promises sounded empty and unconvincing.
4. **Opposite Words:** sincere, thoughtful
5. **GRE Synonyms:** slick, facile

**12. headstrong**
1. **Definition:** Self-willed and obstinate.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Stubbornly independent; willful
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her **headstrong** nature often led her to make impulsive decisions.
    *  The **headstrong** child refused to listen to his parents' advice.
4. **Opposite Words:** docile, compliant
5. **GRE Synonyms:** obstinate, recalcitrant

**13. intermittent**
1. **Definition:** Occurring at irregular intervals; not continuous or steady.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Occurring at intervals; sporadic
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **intermittent** rain showers continued throughout the day.
    *  There were **intermittent** power outages during the storm.
4. **Opposite Words:** continuous, constant
5. **GRE Synonyms:** sporadic, periodic

**14. ire**
1. **Definition:** Anger.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Intense anger; wrath
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The unfair decision provoked his **ire**.
    *  Public **ire** erupted after the scandal was revealed.
4. **Opposite Words:** placidity, peace
5. **GRE Synonyms:** wrath, fury

**15. languid(1)**
1. **Definition:** (of a person, animal, or manner) displaying or having a disinclination for physical exertion or effort; slow and relaxed.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Lacking energy; slow moving
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The heat made everyone feel **languid** and lethargic.
    *  She moved with a **languid** grace across the room.
4. **Opposite Words:** energetic, vigorous
5. **GRE Synonyms:** listless, lethargic

**16. languid(2)**
1. **Definition:** Weak or faint from illness or fatigue.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Weak or faint from fatigue
3. **Sentences:**
    *  After the illness, he felt **languid** and unable to exercise.
    *  Her voice was **languid** and barely audible.
4. **Opposite Words:** strong, robust
5. **GRE Synonyms:** feeble, enervated

**17. lull(1)**
1. **Definition:** A temporary interval of quiet or lack of activity.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Temporary pause in activity
3. **Sentences:**
    *  There was a brief **lull** in the fighting.
    *  The conversation fell into a **lull** as people waited for the news.
4. **Opposite Words:** surge, intensification
5. **GRE Synonyms:** respite, hiatus

**18. lull(2)**
1. **Definition:** Calm or send to sleep, typically with soothing sounds or movements.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To soothe or calm; pacify
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The gentle music **lulled** the baby to sleep.
    *  The calm words **lulled** her fears temporarily.
4. **Opposite Words:** agitate, provoke
5. **GRE Synonyms:** pacify, soothe

**19. mettlesome**
1. **Definition:** (of a person or animal) full of spirit and courage.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Courageous; spirited; valiant
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **mettlesome** knight charged bravely into battle.
    *  She is a **mettlesome** competitor, never backing down from a challenge.
4. **Opposite Words:** cowardly, timid
5. **GRE Synonyms:** valiant, intrepid

**20. mollify**
1. **Definition:** Appease the anger or anxiety of (someone).
2. **Concise Meaning:** To soothe or appease anger
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He tried to **mollify** his angry customer with an apology.
    *  The negotiator attempted to **mollify** both sides in the dispute.
4. **Opposite Words:** aggravate, provoke
5. **GRE Synonyms:** appease, placate

**21. neutralize**
1. **Definition:** Render (something) ineffective or harmless by counteracting its effects.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To counteract or make ineffective
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The antidote will **neutralize** the poison's effects.
    *  He tried to **neutralize** the negative publicity with positive stories.
4. **Opposite Words:** activate, intensify
5. **GRE Synonyms:** counteract, negate

**22. nonplussed**
1. **Definition:** (of a person) surprised and confused so much that they are unsure how to react.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Confused and unsure how to react
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She was **nonplussed** by his sudden change of mood.
    *  The unexpected question left him completely **nonplussed**.
4. **Opposite Words:** composed, assured
5. **GRE Synonyms:** bewildered, perplexed

**23. precipitous(1)**
1. **Definition:** Dangerously high or steep.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Dangerously steep or high
3. **Sentences:**
    *  They cautiously climbed the **precipitous** cliff face.
    *  The road had a **precipitous** drop on one side.
4. **Opposite Words:** gradual, gentle
5. **GRE Synonyms:** sheer, abrupt

**24. precipitous(2)**
1. **Definition:** (of a decrease) sudden and dramatic.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Sudden and dramatic decrease
3. **Sentences:**
    *  There was a **precipitous** decline in sales after the scandal.
    *  The stock market experienced a **precipitous** fall.
4. **Opposite Words:** gradual, incremental
5. **GRE Synonyms:** abrupt, sharp

**25. pretentious**
1. **Definition:** Attempting to impress by affecting greater importance, talent, culture, etc., than is actually possessed.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Showy; claiming false importance
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **pretentious** language annoyed everyone at the party.
    *  The restaurant's **pretentious** decor didn't match the mediocre food.
4. **Opposite Words:** humble, modest
5. **GRE Synonyms:** ostentatious, pompous

**26. profound(1)**
1. **Definition:** (of a state, quality, or emotion) very great or intense.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Very great or intense feeling
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She felt a **profound** sense of sadness at his departure.
    *  The experience had a **profound** impact on his life.
4. **Opposite Words:** superficial, shallow
5. **GRE Synonyms:** intense, deep

**27. profound(2)**
1. **Definition:** Having or showing great knowledge or insight.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Deeply insightful or knowledgeable
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **profound** understanding of philosophy was evident in his lecture.
    *  She offered a **profound** analysis of the political situation.
4. **Opposite Words:** ignorant, superficial
5. **GRE Synonyms:** insightful, erudite

**28. propagate**
1. **Definition:** Spread and promote (an idea, theory, etc.) widely.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To spread or promote widely
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The internet helps to **propagate** information quickly.
    *  They **propagate** rumors without checking their validity.
4. **Opposite Words:** suppress, contain
5. **GRE Synonyms:** disseminate, promulgate

**29. recourse**
1. **Definition:** A source of help in a difficult situation.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Source of help; option
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Mediation is often the first **recourse** in resolving disputes.
    *  When all else fails, legal action is the final **recourse**.
4. **Opposite Words:** impasse, dead end
5. **GRE Synonyms:** resort, expedient

**30. refute**
1. **Definition:** Prove (a statement or theory) to be wrong or false; disprove.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To disprove or prove false
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The scientist **refuted** the earlier claims with new evidence.
    *  He attempted to **refute** the accusations made against him.
4. **Opposite Words:** confirm, validate
5. **GRE Synonyms:** rebut, invalidate

**31. regress**
1. **Definition:** Return to a former or less developed state.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To return to worse state
3. **Sentences:**
    *  After a period of improvement, his health began to **regress**.
    *  The economy may **regress** if the policies are not effective.
4. **Opposite Words:** progress, advance
5. **GRE Synonyms:** revert, relapse

**32. repercussion**
1. **Definition:** An unintended consequence of an event or action, especially an unwelcome one.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Unintended consequence; after-effect
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The decision had serious **repercussions** for the company's future.
    *  There were unforeseen **repercussions** of the new law.
4. **Opposite Words:** cause, antecedent
5. **GRE Synonyms:** consequence, ramification

**33. replenish**
1. **Definition:** Restore (something depleted) to a former level or condition.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To refill or restore; restock
3. **Sentences:**
    *  We need to **replenish** our supplies before the journey.
    *  Drinking water helps to **replenish** fluids lost during exercise.
4. **Opposite Words:** deplete, exhaust
5. **GRE Synonyms:** restore, restock

**34. vigilant**
1. **Definition:** Keeping careful watch for possible danger or difficulties.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Watchful; alert to danger
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Security guards must remain **vigilant** at all times.
    *  The public should be **vigilant** against scams and fraud.
4. **Opposite Words:** negligent, inattentive
5. **GRE Synonyms:** watchful, alert

# 24
Okay, I will provide the information for each word in your list according to your instructions.

**1. assail**
1. **Definition:** Attack violently.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Violently attack or criticize
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Critics **assailed** the author's new book.
    *  The enemy **assailed** the fort with heavy fire.
4. **Opposite Words:** defend, protect
5. **GRE Synonyms:** lambast, impugn

**2. benevolent**
1. **Definition:** Well meaning and kindly.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Kind, charitable, and well-meaning
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **benevolent** donor funded the new hospital wing.
    *  Her **benevolent** smile put everyone at ease.
4. **Opposite Words:** malevolent, unkind
5. **GRE Synonyms:** altruistic, magnanimous

**3. berate**
1. **Definition:** Scold or criticize (someone) angrily.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Scold or criticize angrily
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The boss **berated** the employee for being late.
    *  She **berated** herself for making such a silly mistake.
4. **Opposite Words:** praise, commend
5. **GRE Synonyms:** castigate, upbraid

**4. buoyant**
1. **Definition:** (1) Able to stay afloat or rise to the top of a liquid or gas. (2) Cheerful and optimistic.
2. **Concise Meaning:** (1) Able to float. (2) Cheerful, optimistic
3. **Sentences:**
    *  (1) The life jacket is **buoyant** enough to keep you safe.
    *  (2) Her **buoyant** personality lifted everyone's spirits.
4. **Opposite Words:** (1) heavy, sinking (2) depressed, pessimistic
5. **GRE Synonyms:** (1) floatable, resilient (2) ebullient, sanguine

**5. buttress**
1. **Definition:** (1) A projecting support of stone or brick built against a wall. (2) Increase the strength of or justification for; reinforce.
2. **Concise Meaning:** (1) Wall support. (2) Strengthen, reinforce
3. **Sentences:**
    *  (1) The cathedral's walls have strong **buttresses**.
    *  (2)  New evidence **buttressed** his claim of innocence.
4. **Opposite Words:** (2) undermine, weaken
5. **GRE Synonyms:** (2) bolster, fortify

**6. condone**
1. **Definition:** Accept and allow (behaviour that is considered morally wrong or offensive) to continue.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Accept or allow wrong behavior
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The school does not **condone** bullying of any kind.
    *  I cannot **condone** such disrespectful behavior.
4. **Opposite Words:** condemn, forbid
5. **GRE Synonyms:** excuse, overlook

**7. contravene**
1. **Definition:** Violate the prohibition or order of (a law, treaty, or code of conduct).
2. **Concise Meaning:** Violate or go against law
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His actions **contravened** the company policy.
    *  The new law **contravenes** basic human rights.
4. **Opposite Words:** uphold, obey
5. **GRE Synonyms:** infringe, transgress

**8. denounce**
1. **Definition:** Publicly declare to be wrong or evil.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Publicly condemn as wrong
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The politician **denounced** the corruption scandal.
    *  Human rights groups **denounced** the violent crackdown.
4. **Opposite Words:** praise, commend
5. **GRE Synonyms:** censure, vilify

**9. despotic**
1. **Definition:** Of or relating to a despot; tyrannical.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Tyrannical, autocratic, dictatorial
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **despotic** ruler controlled every aspect of life.
    *  His **despotic** management style stifled creativity.
4. **Opposite Words:** democratic, lenient
5. **GRE Synonyms:** authoritarian, autocratic

**10. deviate**
1. **Definition:** Depart from an established course.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Depart from usual course
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Do not **deviate** from the set path.
    *  Her opinions **deviate** from the mainstream view.
4. **Opposite Words:** conform, adhere
5. **GRE Synonyms:** diverge, stray

**11. disinterested**
1. **Definition:** Not influenced by personal feelings, opinions, or concerns.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Impartial, unbiased, objective
3. **Sentences:**
    *  A judge should be **disinterested** in the case.
    *  We need a **disinterested** third party to mediate.
4. **Opposite Words:** biased, partial
5. **GRE Synonyms:** impartial, detached

**12. escalate**
1. **Definition:** Increase rapidly.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Increase or intensify rapidly
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The conflict began to **escalate** into a full-scale war.
    *  The prices **escalated** due to high demand.
4. **Opposite Words:** decrease, diminish
5. **GRE Synonyms:** intensify, augment

**13. exorcise**
1. **Definition:** Drive out or attempt to drive out (an evil spirit) from a person or place.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Drive out evil spirit
3. **Sentences:**
    *  They tried to **exorcise** the demon from the possessed girl.
    *  He needed to **exorcise** the negative thoughts from his mind.
4. **Opposite Words:** invite, welcome (spirit)
5. **GRE Synonyms:** expel, purge

**14. finicky**
1. **Definition:** Fussy about their needs or requirements.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Fussy, picky, fastidious
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The child is a **finicky** eater and dislikes most vegetables.
    *  He was **finicky** about the cleanliness of his workspace.
4. **Opposite Words:** easygoing, undemanding
5. **GRE Synonyms:** fastidious, meticulous

**15. foil**
1. **Definition:** Prevent (something considered wrong or undesirable) from succeeding.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Prevent, thwart, frustrate plans
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The police **foiled** the bank robbery attempt.
    *  Her clever plan **foiled** his evil scheme.
4. **Opposite Words:** aid, assist
5. **GRE Synonyms:** thwart, stymie

**16. intertwined**
1. **Definition:** Connected or linked closely.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Closely connected or linked
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Their fates are **intertwined** forever.
    *  The two storylines are intricately **intertwined**.
4. **Opposite Words:** separate, detached
5. **GRE Synonyms:** interwoven, entangled

**17. inundate**
1. **Definition:** Overwhelm (someone) with things or people to be dealt with.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Overwhelm with excessive amount
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The office was **inundated** with emails after the announcement.
    *  The coastal town was **inundated** by the floodwaters.
4. **Opposite Words:** deplete, drain
5. **GRE Synonyms:** deluge, overwhelm

**18. ironclad**
1. **Definition:** Impossible to contradict, weaken, or change.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Unbreakable, firm, indisputable
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The contract provided **ironclad** guarantees.
    *  He had an **ironclad** alibi for the night of the crime.
4. **Opposite Words:** weak, vulnerable
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  indisputable, impregnable

**19. jeopardize**
1. **Definition:** Put (someone or something) into a situation in which there is a danger of loss, harm, or failure.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Put in danger, risk
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His reckless driving **jeopardized** everyone's safety.
    *  Don't **jeopardize** your future by making rash decisions.
4. **Opposite Words:** protect, safeguard
5. **GRE Synonyms:** imperil, endanger

**20. mercurial**
1. **Definition:** Subject to sudden or unpredictable changes of mood or mind.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Unpredictable, quickly changing moods
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her **mercurial** temperament made her difficult to work with.
    *  The stock market is known for its **mercurial** nature.
4. **Opposite Words:** stable, constant
5. **GRE Synonyms:** volatile, capricious

**21. oblivious**
1. **Definition:** Not aware of or not concerned about what is happening around one.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Unaware, unconscious, unmindful
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He was **oblivious** to the danger around him.
    *  Lost in thought, she was **oblivious** to the noise.
4. **Opposite Words:** aware, conscious
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  unmindful, insensible

**22. perpetrate**
1. **Definition:** Carry out or commit (a harmful, illegal, or immoral action).
2. **Concise Meaning:** Commit harmful or illegal act
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He was accused of **perpetrating** the fraud.
    *  They **perpetrated** a series of violent crimes.
4. **Opposite Words:** prevent, deter
5. **GRE Synonyms:** commit, execute

**23. plaintive**
1. **Definition:** Sounding sad and mournful.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Sad, mournful, expressing sorrow
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The dove cooed with a **plaintive** cry.
    *  Her voice was **plaintive** as she spoke of her loss.
4. **Opposite Words:** joyful, cheerful
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  melancholy, lugubrious

**24. poignant**
1. **Definition:** Evoking a keen sense of sadness or regret.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Touching, evoking sadness, regret
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The movie ended with a **poignant** scene that made everyone cry.
    *  Her letter was a **poignant** reminder of lost love.
4. **Opposite Words:**  joyful, cheerful
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  bittersweet, moving

**25. quiescent**
1. **Definition:** In a state or period of inactivity or dormancy.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Inactive, dormant, still
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The volcano has been **quiescent** for centuries.
    *  After the storm, the sea became **quiescent**.
4. **Opposite Words:** active, agitated
5. **GRE Synonyms:** dormant, latent

**26. reiterate**
1. **Definition:** Say something again or a number of times, typically for emphasis or clarity.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Repeat for emphasis, clarify
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Let me **reiterate** the importance of punctuality.
    *  The teacher **reiterated** the instructions for the assignment.
4. **Opposite Words:** retract, recant
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  recapitulate, restate

**27. subside**
1. **Definition:** Become less intense, violent, or severe.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Lessen, decrease in intensity
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The storm began to **subside** in the evening.
    *  His anger gradually **subsided** as he calmed down.
4. **Opposite Words:** intensify, increase
5. **GRE Synonyms:** abate, dwindle

**28. subsume**
1. **Definition:** Absorb or include (something) under a larger category.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Include or absorb into larger group
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Individual rights are often **subsumed** by national interests.
    *  The smaller company was **subsumed** into the larger corporation.
4. **Opposite Words:** separate, differentiate
5. **GRE Synonyms:** incorporate, encompass

**29. surmount**
1. **Definition:** Overcome (a difficulty or obstacle).
2. **Concise Meaning:** Overcome, conquer obstacles
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She had to **surmount** many challenges to succeed.
    *  They **surmounted** their initial difficulties and thrived.
4. **Opposite Words:** succumb, yield
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  overcome, conquer

**30. tangential**
1. **Definition:** Relating to or along a tangent; diverging from the main point.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Diverging from main point, unrelated
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His comments were **tangential** to the main discussion.
    *  The side story is **tangential** to the central plot.
4. **Opposite Words:** relevant, pertinent
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  peripheral, extraneous

# 25
**1. adept**
1. **Definition:** Very skilled or proficient at something.
2. **Concise Meaning:** highly skilled or proficient
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She is **adept** at handling difficult customers.
    *  He became **adept** in coding after years of practice.
4. **Opposite Words:** inept, unskilled
5. **GRE Synonyms:** proficient, skillful

**2. adverse**
1. **Definition:** Preventing success or development; harmful or unfavourable.
2. **Concise Meaning:** unfavorable, harmful, opposing
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The company faced **adverse** economic conditions.
    *  His health suffered due to the **adverse** side effects of the medication.
4. **Opposite Words:** favorable, beneficial
5. **GRE Synonyms:** detrimental, inimical

**3. appropriate (1)**
1. **Definition:** Suitable or proper in the circumstances.
2. **Concise Meaning:** suitable or proper for situation
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Formal attire is **appropriate** for the wedding.
    *  His comments were not **appropriate** for a professional setting.
4. **Opposite Words:** unsuitable, improper
5. **GRE Synonyms:** fitting, apt

**4. appropriate (2)**
1. **Definition:** Take (something) for one's own use, typically without the owner's permission.
2. **Concise Meaning:** take for own use, steal
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He was accused of **appropriating** company funds.
    *  The artist **appropriated** images from popular culture in her work.
4. **Opposite Words:** relinquish, return
5. **GRE Synonyms:** pilfer, usurp

**5. archetype**
1. **Definition:** A very typical example of a certain person or thing.
2. **Concise Meaning:** typical example or model
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Sherlock Holmes is the **archetype** of a detective.
    *  The hero's journey is a common **archetype** in literature.
4. **Opposite Words:** anomaly, deviation
5. **GRE Synonyms:** prototype, paradigm

**6. articulate**
1. **Definition:** Express (an idea or feeling) fluently and coherently.
2. **Concise Meaning:** express clearly and fluently
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She can **articulate** her thoughts very effectively.
    *  He struggled to **articulate** his complex feelings.
4. **Opposite Words:** inarticulate, incoherent
5. **GRE Synonyms:** eloquent, lucid

**7. auspicious**
1. **Definition:** Conducive to success; favourable.
2. **Concise Meaning:** favorable, promising success
3. **Sentences:**
    *  It was an **auspicious** start to the business venture.
    *  They chose an **auspicious** date for their wedding.
4. **Opposite Words:** inauspicious, unfavorable
5. **GRE Synonyms:** propitious, fortunate

**8. bereft**
1. **Definition:** Deprived of or lacking something, especially a non-material asset.
2. **Concise Meaning:** deprived or lacking something
3. **Sentences:**
    *  After the storm, the trees were **bereft** of leaves.
    *  He felt **bereft** of hope after the bad news.
4. **Opposite Words:** full, replete
5. **GRE Synonyms:** devoid, destitute

**9. captious**
1. **Definition:** Tending to find fault or raise petty objections.
2. **Concise Meaning:** fault-finding, critical, nitpicking
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **captious** critic always found something to complain about.
    *  Don't be so **captious**; appreciate the positive aspects.
4. **Opposite Words:** appreciative, tolerant
5. **GRE Synonyms:** carping, censorious

**10. conclusive**
1. **Definition:** (Of evidence or argument) serving to prove a case; decisive or convincing.
2. **Concise Meaning:** decisive, convincing, proving case
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The DNA evidence was **conclusive** in proving his guilt.
    *  We need **conclusive** proof before making a decision.
4. **Opposite Words:** inconclusive, ambiguous
5. **GRE Synonyms:** definitive, irrefutable

**11. conspire**
1. **Definition:** Make secret plans jointly to commit an unlawful or harmful act.
2. **Concise Meaning:** secretly plan harmful act
3. **Sentences:**
    *  They **conspired** to overthrow the government.
    *  The villains **conspired** against the superhero.
4. **Opposite Words:** collaborate, cooperate
5. **GRE Synonyms:** collude, intrigue

**12. delineate**
1. **Definition:** Describe or portray (something) precisely.
2. **Concise Meaning:** describe precisely, outline
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The speaker **delineated** the steps of the project clearly.
    *  The artist carefully **delineated** the features of the landscape.
4. **Opposite Words:** obscure, confuse
5. **GRE Synonyms:** depict, detail

**13. disentangle**
1. **Definition:** Free (something or someone) from something that they are entangled with.
2. **Concise Meaning:** untangle, free from complication
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She tried to **disentangle** the wires.
    *  He needed to **disentangle** himself from the messy situation.
4. **Opposite Words:** entangle, involve
5. **GRE Synonyms:** extricate, unravel

**14. exhort**
1. **Definition:** Strongly encourage or urge (someone) to do something.
2. **Concise Meaning:** strongly urge or encourage
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The coach **exhorted** the team to give their best.
    *  She **exhorted** him to take responsibility for his actions.
4. **Opposite Words:** discourage, deter
5. **GRE Synonyms:** implore, beseech

**15. frailty**
1. **Definition:** The condition of being weak and delicate.
2. **Concise Meaning:** weakness, delicacy, vulnerability
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **frailty** of the old bridge was concerning.
    *  Human **frailty** is a common theme in literature.
4. **Opposite Words:** strength, robustness
5. **GRE Synonyms:** infirmity, debility

**16. grievance**
1. **Definition:** A real or imagined wrong or other cause for complaint or protest, especially unfair treatment.
2. **Concise Meaning:** complaint, cause for protest
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The workers filed a **grievance** about unfair wages.
    *  He harbored a deep **grievance** against his former boss.
4. **Opposite Words:** satisfaction, contentment
5. **GRE Synonyms:** complaint, umbrage

**17. harangue**
1. **Definition:** A lengthy and aggressive speech.
2. **Concise Meaning:** aggressive, lengthy, critical speech
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The politician delivered a fiery **harangue** against his opponents.
    *  She launched into a **harangue** about the state of society.
4. **Opposite Words:** eulogy, praise
5. **GRE Synonyms:** tirade, diatribe

**18. ploy**
1. **Definition:** A cunning plan or action designed to turn a situation to one's own advantage.
2. **Concise Meaning:** cunning plan, strategic trick
3. **Sentences:**
    *  It was a clever **ploy** to distract the guards.
    *  His sudden illness was just a **ploy** to avoid work.
4. **Opposite Words:** honesty, candor
5. **GRE Synonyms:** stratagem, ruse

**19. poise**
1. **Definition:** Graceful and elegant manner.
2. **Concise Meaning:** graceful, elegant manner, composure
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She carried herself with remarkable **poise**.
    *  Despite the pressure, he maintained his **poise**.
4. **Opposite Words:** awkwardness, agitation
5. **GRE Synonyms:** equanimity, aplomb

**20. pomposity**
1. **Definition:** The quality of being pompous; self-importance.
2. **Concise Meaning:** self-importance, arrogance, pretension
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **pomposity** made him difficult to work with.
    *  The speech was full of **pomposity** and empty rhetoric.
4. **Opposite Words:** humility, modesty
5. **GRE Synonyms:** grandiloquence, pretension

**21. proxy**
1. **Definition:** Authority to represent someone else, especially in voting.
2. **Concise Meaning:** substitute, representative, agent
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He voted by **proxy** in the shareholder meeting.
    *  She acted as his **proxy** in the negotiations.
4. **Opposite Words:** principal, original
5. **GRE Synonyms:** delegate, surrogate

**22. relent (1)**
1. **Definition:** Abandon or mitigate a harsh intention or cruel treatment.
2. **Concise Meaning:** soften, become less harsh
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The storm finally **relented** after days of heavy rain.
    *  The strict teacher **relented** and allowed extra time.
4. **Opposite Words:** persist, intensify
5. **GRE Synonyms:** yield, acquiesce

**23. relent (2)**
1. **Definition:** Become less severe or intense.
2. **Concise Meaning:** become less intense, ease up
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The pressure on him did not **relent**.
    *  The pain in her leg finally **relented** after medication.
4. **Opposite Words:** intensify, worsen
5. **GRE Synonyms:** abate, subside

**24. rhetoric**
1. **Definition:** The art of effective or persuasive speaking or writing, especially the use of figures of speech and other compositional techniques.
2. **Concise Meaning:** persuasive speaking or writing art
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His speech was full of powerful **rhetoric**.
    *  The politician used emotional **rhetoric** to sway voters.
4. **Opposite Words:** conciseness, directness
5. **GRE Synonyms:** oratory, eloquence

**25. rigor**
1. **Definition:** Severity or strictness.
2. **Concise Meaning:** strictness, severity, harshness
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **rigor** of the training was demanding.
    *  Scientific research requires intellectual **rigor**.
4. **Opposite Words:** leniency, laxity
5. **GRE Synonyms:** austerity, stringency

**26. sparse**
1. **Definition:** Thinly dispersed or scattered.
2. **Concise Meaning:** thinly scattered, not dense
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Vegetation was **sparse** in the desert.
    *  The crowd was **sparse** due to the rain.
4. **Opposite Words:** abundant, dense
5. **GRE Synonyms:** meager, scant

**27. steadfast**
1. **Definition:** Resolutely or dutifully firm and unwavering.
2. **Concise Meaning:** firm, unwavering, resolute
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He remained **steadfast** in his beliefs.
    *  Her loyalty was **steadfast** throughout their friendship.
4. **Opposite Words:** wavering, fickle
5. **GRE Synonyms:** resolute, staunch

**28. suspect**
1. **Definition:** Have an idea or impression of the existence, presence, or truth of (something) without certain proof.
2. **Concise Meaning:** doubt, question, mistrust
3. **Sentences:**
    *  I **suspect** he is lying about his age.
    *  Police **suspect** foul play in the disappearance.
4. **Opposite Words:** trust, believe
5. **GRE Synonyms:** conjecture, surmise

**29. tedious**
1. **Definition:** Too long, slow, or dull; tiresome or monotonous.
2. **Concise Meaning:** boring, monotonous, tiresome
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The lecture was long and **tedious**.
    *  Repetitive tasks can become very **tedious**.
4. **Opposite Words:** interesting, engaging
5. **GRE Synonyms:** monotonous, irksome

**30. vitality**
1. **Definition:** The state of being strong and active; energy.
2. **Concise Meaning:** energy, liveliness, vigor
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She is full of **vitality** and enthusiasm.
    *  Exercise improves overall **vitality**.
4. **Opposite Words:** lethargy, weakness
5. **GRE Synonyms:** vigor, animation

**31. whimsical (1)**
1. **Definition:** Acting or behaving in a capricious manner.
2. **Concise Meaning:** capricious, playful, unpredictable
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her **whimsical** nature made her fun to be around.
    *  He made a **whimsical** decision to quit his job.
4. **Opposite Words:** serious, pragmatic
5. **GRE Synonyms:** capricious, erratic

**32. whimsical (2)**
1. **Definition:** Playfully quaint or fanciful, especially in an appealing and amusing way.
2. **Concise Meaning:** fanciful, amusingly unusual
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The garden was decorated with **whimsical** statues.
    *  She had a **whimsical** sense of style.
4. **Opposite Words:** ordinary, conventional
5. **GRE Synonyms:** fanciful, quaint

**33. yield (1)**
1. **Definition:** Produce or provide (a natural, agricultural, or industrial product).
2. **Concise Meaning:** produce, generate, provide
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The farm will **yield** a good harvest this year.
    *  Investments should **yield** high returns.
4. **Opposite Words:** consume, deplete
5. **GRE Synonyms:** generate, produce

**34. yield (2)**
1. **Definition:** Give way to arguments, demands, or pressure.
2. **Concise Meaning:** give in, surrender, concede
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He refused to **yield** to their demands.
    *  She finally **yielded** under the pressure of questioning.
4. **Opposite Words:** resist, withstand
5. **GRE Synonyms:** succumb, capitulate

# 26
Okay, I will provide the definitions, concise meanings, sentences, opposite words and synonyms for each word in your list, following your instructions and format.

**1. apprehension**
1. **Definition:** Anxiety or fear that something bad or unpleasant will happen.
2. **Concise Meaning:** anxiety or fear of future
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Despite her initial **apprehension**, the roller coaster turned out to be exhilarating.
    *  There is growing **apprehension** about the future of the economy.
4. **Opposite Words:** confidence, composure
5. **GRE Synonyms:** trepidation, foreboding

**2. ardent**
1. **Definition:** Very enthusiastic or passionate.
2. **Concise Meaning:** passionate; intensely enthusiastic
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He was an **ardent** supporter of animal rights.
    *  Her **ardent** love for music was evident in every performance.
4. **Opposite Words:** apathetic, indifferent
5. **GRE Synonyms:** fervent, zealous

**3. axiomatic**
1. **Definition:** Self-evident or unquestionable.
2. **Concise Meaning:** self-evident; obviously true
3. **Sentences:**
    *  It is **axiomatic** that prices will rise during periods of inflation.
    *  The principle of fairness is considered **axiomatic** in many legal systems.
4. **Opposite Words:** questionable, dubious
5. **GRE Synonyms:** self-evident, undeniable

**4. cease**
1. **Definition:** Come or bring to an end.
2. **Concise Meaning:** stop; come to an end
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The rain will **cease** by morning.
    *  Negotiations must **cease** if violence continues.
4. **Opposite Words:** begin, commence
5. **GRE Synonyms:** terminate, halt

**5. conducive**
1. **Definition:** Making a certain situation or outcome likely or possible.
2. **Concise Meaning:** favorable to; promoting
3. **Sentences:**
    *  A quiet environment is **conducive** to studying.
    *  These policies are **conducive** to economic growth.
4. **Opposite Words:** hindering, obstructive
5. **GRE Synonyms:** beneficial, propitious

**6. corporeal**
1. **Definition:** Relating to a person's body, especially as opposed to their spirit.
2. **Concise Meaning:** bodily; physical; tangible
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Ghosts are not **corporeal** beings.
    *  The pain was not just emotional but also **corporeal**.
4. **Opposite Words:** incorporeal, spiritual
5. **GRE Synonyms:** bodily, tangible

**7. doctrinaire**
1. **Definition:** Seeking to impose a doctrine in all circumstances without regard to practical considerations.
2. **Concise Meaning:** rigidly applying doctrines/theories
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **doctrinaire** approach to politics left no room for compromise.
    *  The professor's **doctrinaire** views were often challenged by students.
4. **Opposite Words:** pragmatic, flexible
5. **GRE Synonyms:** dogmatic, ideological

**8. eclectic**
1. **Definition:** Deriving ideas, style, or taste from a broad and diverse range of sources.
2. **Concise Meaning:** diverse sources; wide-ranging
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her music taste is **eclectic**, ranging from classical to rock.
    *  The restaurant's menu is **eclectic**, featuring dishes from many cultures.
4. **Opposite Words:** narrow, uniform
5. **GRE Synonyms:** diverse, varied

**9. equanimity**
1. **Definition:** Mental calmness, composure, and evenness of temper, especially in a difficult situation.
2. **Concise Meaning:** calmness; composure; even temper
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She faced the crisis with remarkable **equanimity**.
    *  Despite the chaos, he maintained his **equanimity**.
4. **Opposite Words:** agitation, perturbation
5. **GRE Synonyms:** composure, serenity

**10. exorbitant**
1. **Definition:** (of a price or amount charged) unreasonably high.
2. **Concise Meaning:** unreasonably high; excessive
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The hotel charged an **exorbitant** price for a simple room.
    *  Consumers complained about the **exorbitant** fees.
4. **Opposite Words:** reasonable, moderate
5. **GRE Synonyms:** excessive, extravagant

**11. fickle**
1. **Definition:** Changing frequently, especially as regards one's loyalties or affections.
2. **Concise Meaning:** changeable; inconstant; capricious
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The weather is notoriously **fickle** in this region.
    *  Her **fickle** loyalties made her unreliable.
4. **Opposite Words:** constant, steadfast
5. **GRE Synonyms:** capricious, volatile

**12. figurative**
1. **Definition:** Departing from a literal use of words; metaphorical.
2. **Concise Meaning:** metaphorical; not literal
3. **Sentences:**
    *  "Heart of stone" is a **figurative** expression.
    *  The poem uses **figurative** language to create vivid imagery.
4. **Opposite Words:** literal, actual
5. **GRE Synonyms:** metaphorical, symbolic

**13. flustered**
1. **Definition:** Make (someone) agitated or confused.
2. **Concise Meaning:** agitated; confused; rattled
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He became **flustered** when asked a difficult question.
    *  The unexpected phone call left her feeling **flustered**.
4. **Opposite Words:** composed, collected
5. **GRE Synonyms:** agitated, discomposed

**14. gullible**
1. **Definition:** Easily persuaded to believe something; credulous.
2. **Concise Meaning:** easily fooled; naive; credulous
3. **Sentences:**
    *  **Gullible** people are easy targets for scams.
    *  He was **gullible** enough to believe the unbelievable story.
4. **Opposite Words:** skeptical, astute
5. **GRE Synonyms:** credulous, naive

**15. idiosyncratic**
1. **Definition:** Peculiar or individual.
2. **Concise Meaning:** peculiar; unique; individualistic
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **idiosyncratic** style of dressing made him stand out.
    *  She had some **idiosyncratic** habits that amused her friends.
4. **Opposite Words:** conventional, typical
5. **GRE Synonyms:** peculiar, eccentric

**16. incidental**
1. **Definition:** Occurring as a minor accompaniment to something else.
2. **Concise Meaning:** minor; secondary; not essential
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The meeting was delayed due to **incidental** issues.
    *  His comments were **incidental** to the main topic.
4. **Opposite Words:** essential, primary
5. **GRE Synonyms:** secondary, subordinate

**17. ingrained**
1. **Definition:** (of a habit, belief, or attitude) firmly fixed or established; difficult to change.
2. **Concise Meaning:** deeply fixed; firmly established
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The habit of politeness was **ingrained** in her from childhood.
    *  Racism is deeply **ingrained** in some societies.
4. **Opposite Words:** superficial, extrinsic
5. **GRE Synonyms:** entrenched, deep-rooted

**18. insolent**
1. **Definition:** Showing a rude and arrogant lack of respect.
2. **Concise Meaning:** rude; disrespectful; arrogant
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The student was punished for his **insolent** behavior towards the teacher.
    *  His **insolent** tone offended everyone in the room.
4. **Opposite Words:** respectful, deferential
5. **GRE Synonyms:** impudent, impudent

**19. lampoon**
1. **Definition:** Publicly criticize (someone or something) by using ridicule, irony, or sarcasm.
2. **Concise Meaning:** ridicule; satirize publicly
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The comedian **lampooned** politicians in his stand-up routine.
    *  The article **lampooned** the absurdities of modern art.
4. **Opposite Words:** praise, commend
5. **GRE Synonyms:** satirize, mock

**20. lavish (1)**
1. **Definition:** Sumptuously rich, elaborate, or luxurious.
2. **Concise Meaning:** luxurious; extravagant; abundant
3. **Sentences:**
    *  They lived a **lavish** lifestyle in a mansion.
    *  The wedding was a **lavish** affair with expensive decorations.
4. **Opposite Words:** meager, sparse
5. **GRE Synonyms:** opulent, sumptuous

**21. lavish (2)**
1. **Definition:** Bestow something in generous or extravagant quantities on.
2. **Concise Meaning:** give generously; bestow abundantly
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She **lavished** praise on her students for their hard work.
    *  Nature **lavishes** beauty upon the countryside in springtime.
4. **Opposite Words:** withhold, stint
5. **GRE Synonyms:** bestow, shower

**22. lugubrious**
1. **Definition:** Looking or sounding sad and dismal.
2. **Concise Meaning:** mournful; gloomy; dismal
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **lugubrious** music perfectly matched the rainy weather.
    *  His **lugubrious** expression suggested bad news.
4. **Opposite Words:** cheerful, jovial
5. **GRE Synonyms:** mournful, gloomy

**23. macabre**
1. **Definition:** Disturbing and horrifying because of involvement with or depiction of death and injury.
2. **Concise Meaning:** gruesome; horrifying; death-related
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The movie had a **macabre** scene in the graveyard.
    *  He had a **macabre** fascination with horror stories.
4. **Opposite Words:** pleasant, cheerful
5. **GRE Synonyms:** gruesome, morbid

**24. morose**
1. **Definition:** Sullen and ill-tempered.
2. **Concise Meaning:** sullen; gloomy; bad-tempered
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He was **morose** after failing the exam.
    *  The **morose** atmosphere in the office was palpable.
4. **Opposite Words:** cheerful, optimistic
5. **GRE Synonyms:** sullen, glum

**25. officious**
1. **Definition:** Assertive of authority in an annoyingly domineering way, especially with regard to petty or trivial matters.
2. **Concise Meaning:** meddling; bossy; intrusive
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **officious** waiter kept interrupting our conversation.
    *  Her **officious** nature made her unpopular at work.
4. **Opposite Words:** diffident, unassuming
5. **GRE Synonyms:** meddlesome, intrusive

**26. ramification**
1. **Definition:** A consequence of an action or event, especially when complex or unwelcome.
2. **Concise Meaning:** consequence; result; implication
3. **Sentences:**
    *  We need to consider all the **ramifications** of this decision.
    *  The political scandal had serious **ramifications** for the government.
4. **Opposite Words:** cause, origin
5. **GRE Synonyms:** consequence, implication

**27. serene**
1. **Definition:** Calm, peaceful, and untroubled; tranquil.
2. **Concise Meaning:** calm; peaceful; tranquil
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The lake was **serene** in the early morning mist.
    *  She maintained a **serene** composure despite the stress.
4. **Opposite Words:** agitated, turbulent
5. **GRE Synonyms:** tranquil, placid

**28. supplant**
1. **Definition:** Supersede and replace.
2. **Concise Meaning:** replace; supersede; displace
3. **Sentences:**
    *  New technology is rapidly **supplanting** older methods.
    *  The younger generation will eventually **supplant** their parents in power.
4. **Opposite Words:** retain, preserve
5. **GRE Synonyms:** supersede, displace

**29. tacit**
1. **Definition:** Understood or implied without being stated.
2. **Concise Meaning:** implied; unspoken; understood
3. **Sentences:**
    *  There was a **tacit** agreement between them not to discuss the issue.
    *  Her silence was a **tacit** admission of guilt.
4. **Opposite Words:** explicit, express
5. **GRE Synonyms:** implicit, unspoken

**30. transcend**
1. **Definition:** Be or go beyond the range or limits of (something abstract, typically a conceptual field or division).
2. **Concise Meaning:** go beyond limits; exceed
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His achievements **transcend** ordinary human limits.
    *  Good music can **transcend** cultural barriers.
4. **Opposite Words:** be limited, be restricted
5. **GRE Synonyms:** surpass, exceed

**31. treatise**
1. **Definition:** A written work dealing formally and systematically with a subject.
2. **Concise Meaning:** formal written work; systematic study
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He wrote a lengthy **treatise** on political philosophy.
    *  This **treatise** examines the history of quantum mechanics.
4. **Opposite Words:** article, essay (informal)
5. **GRE Synonyms:** dissertation, monograph
