      "This **treatise** examines the history of quantum mechanics."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "article",
      "essay"
    ],
    "synonyms": [
      "dissertation",
      "monograph"
    ]
  }
]
```


# 27
**1. antagonize**
1. **Definition:** Cause someone to become hostile.
2. **Concise Meaning:** provoke hostility; make enemy
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His insensitive remarks **antagonized** many audience members.
    *  Don't **antagonize** the guard dog; it might bite.
4. **Opposite Words:** appease, placate
5. **GRE Synonyms:** alienate, irritate

**2. barren(1)**
1. **Definition:** (of land) too poor to produce vegetation.
2. **Concise Meaning:** unproductive land; infertile soil
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **barren** desert landscape offered little sustenance.
    *  Years of drought turned the once fertile fields into **barren** wasteland.
4. **Opposite Words:** fertile, productive
5. **GRE Synonyms:** infertile, desolate

**3. barren(2)**
1. **Definition:**  Not producing results or achievements; unproductive.
2. **Concise Meaning:** unproductive; lacking creativity
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her mind felt **barren** of ideas after weeks of stress.
    *  Despite efforts, the negotiations remained **barren**.
4. **Opposite Words:** fruitful, productive
5. **GRE Synonyms:** sterile, unfruitful

**4. bombastic**
1. **Definition:** High-sounding but with little meaning; inflated.
2. **Concise Meaning:** pompous; inflated language
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **bombastic** speech impressed no one with its emptiness.
    *  The politician's **bombastic** rhetoric lacked substance.
4. **Opposite Words:** humble, modest
5. **GRE Synonyms:** grandiloquent, pompous

**5. cajole**
1. **Definition:** Persuade someone to do something by sustained coaxing or flattery.
2. **Concise Meaning:** persuade by flattery; coax
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She tried to **cajole** him into lending her his car.
    *  He **cajoled** his way into getting a better seat.
4. **Opposite Words:** bully, coerce
5. **GRE Synonyms:** wheedle, coax

**6. chary**
1. **Definition:** Cautiously reluctant to do something.
2. **Concise Meaning:** cautious; wary; hesitant
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She was **chary** of investing her money in the risky venture.
    *  Be **chary** of strangers offering unsolicited advice.
4. **Opposite Words:** reckless, incautious
5. **GRE Synonyms:** circumspect, prudent

**7. curmudgeon**
1. **Definition:** A bad-tempered or surly person.
2. **Concise Meaning:** bad-tempered, grumpy person
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The old man was known as a neighborhood **curmudgeon**.
    *  Despite his **curmudgeon** persona, he had a kind heart.
4. **Opposite Words:** amiable, genial
5. **GRE Synonyms:** grouch, crank

**8. dirge**
1. **Definition:** A lament for the dead, especially one forming part of a funeral rite.
2. **Concise Meaning:** funeral song; mournful lament
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The bagpipes played a mournful **dirge** at the ceremony.
    *  Her poem was a poignant **dirge** for lost youth.
4. **Opposite Words:** paean, anthem
5. **GRE Synonyms:** elegy, lament

**9. estimable**
1. **Definition:** Worthy of great respect.
2. **Concise Meaning:** worthy of respect; admirable
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her contributions to science are **estimable**.
    *  He is an **estimable** member of the community.
4. **Opposite Words:** contemptible, despicable
5. **GRE Synonyms:** venerable, reputable

**10. euphemism**
1. **Definition:** A mild or indirect word or expression substituted for one considered to be too harsh or blunt when referring to something unpleasant or embarrassing.
2. **Concise Meaning:** mild word for harsh thing
3. **Sentences:**
    *  "Passed away" is a common **euphemism** for "died".
    *  Using **euphemisms** can soften difficult conversations.
4. **Opposite Words:** dysphemism, direct term
5. **GRE Synonyms:** circumlocution, delicacy

**11. excoriate**
1. **Definition:** Censure or criticize severely.
2. **Concise Meaning:** criticize severely; denounce
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The media **excoriated** the politician for his scandal.
    *  The teacher **excoriated** the students for their plagiarism.
4. **Opposite Words:** praise, commend
5. **GRE Synonyms:** castigate, lambaste

**12. exigent**
1. **Definition:** Pressing; demanding.
2. **Concise Meaning:** urgent; demanding attention
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The situation was **exigent**, requiring immediate action.
    *  **Exigent** circumstances forced them to evacuate.
4. **Opposite Words:** trivial, unimportant
5. **GRE Synonyms:** critical, imperative

**13. haughty**
1. **Definition:** Arrogantly superior and disdainful.
2. **Concise Meaning:** arrogant; disdainfully proud
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She gave a **haughty** look to the waiter.
    *  His **haughty** demeanor made him unpopular.
4. **Opposite Words:** humble, modest
5. **GRE Synonyms:** supercilious, imperious

**14. heady(1)**
1. **Definition:** (of alcoholic drink) potent; intoxicating.
2. **Concise Meaning:** intoxicating; potent alcohol
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **heady** wine made him feel lightheaded.
    *  Be careful, this punch is quite **heady**.
4. **Opposite Words:** weak, mild
5. **GRE Synonyms:** inebriating, strong

**15. heady(2)**
1. **Definition:** (of an emotion or atmosphere) exciting; exhilarating.
2. **Concise Meaning:** exciting; exhilarating; thrilling
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The victory was a **heady** experience for the team.
    *  Success brought a **heady** feeling of power.
4. **Opposite Words:** calming, depressing
5. **GRE Synonyms:** exhilarating, intoxicating

**16. imperturbable**
1. **Definition:** Not easily perturbed or excited; calm and collected.
2. **Concise Meaning:** calm; unexcitable; unflappable
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The experienced pilot remained **imperturbable** during turbulence.
    *  Her **imperturbable** nature was admired by all.
4. **Opposite Words:** excitable, agitated
5. **GRE Synonyms:** placid, serene

**17. implacable**
1. **Definition:** Unable to be placated; relentless.
2. **Concise Meaning:** relentless; unstoppable; unforgiving
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The dictator was an **implacable** foe of democracy.
    *  His anger was **implacable**, and he refused to forgive.
4. **Opposite Words:** placable, forgiving
5. **GRE Synonyms:** inexorable, unyielding

**18. lambaste**
1. **Definition:** Criticize (someone or something) harshly.
2. **Concise Meaning:** criticize harshly; berate
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The critic **lambasted** the movie for its poor acting.
    *  The coach **lambasted** the team after their defeat.
4. **Opposite Words:** praise, commend
5. **GRE Synonyms:** excoriate, castigate

**19. miscreant**
1. **Definition:** A person who behaves badly or in a way that breaks the law.
2. **Concise Meaning:** villain; evildoer; wrongdoer
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **miscreant** was apprehended by the police.
    *  He was labeled a **miscreant** for his dishonest actions.
4. **Opposite Words:** saint, virtuous person
5. **GRE Synonyms:** reprobate, villain

**20. peccadillo**
1. **Definition:** A relatively minor fault or sin.
2. **Concise Meaning:** minor sin; small fault
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Lying about his age was just a **peccadillo**.
    *  Her occasional lateness was considered a **peccadillo**.
4. **Opposite Words:** felony, major sin
5. **GRE Synonyms:** foible, lapse

**21. philistine**
1. **Definition:** A person who is hostile or indifferent to culture and the arts, or who is smugly conventional.
2. **Concise Meaning:** uncultured person; indifferent to art
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He called anyone who liked pop music a **philistine**.
    *  The **philistine** dismissed the painting as meaningless.
4. **Opposite Words:** connoisseur, cultured person
5. **GRE Synonyms:** boor, barbarian

**22. relegate**
1. **Definition:** Dismiss to an inferior rank or position.
2. **Concise Meaning:** assign to lower position
3. **Sentences:**
    *  After the scandal, he was **relegated** to a minor role.
    *  They **relegated** the old furniture to the basement.
4. **Opposite Words:** promote, elevate
5. **GRE Synonyms:** demote, downgrade

**23. repugnant**
1. **Definition:** Extremely distasteful; unacceptable.
2. **Concise Meaning:** disgusting; repulsive; offensive
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The idea of eating insects was **repugnant** to her.
    *  His behavior was morally **repugnant**.
4. **Opposite Words:** appealing, attractive
5. **GRE Synonyms:** abhorrent, odious

**24. sentimental**
1. **Definition:** Characterized by or expressive of feelings of tenderness, sadness, or nostalgia, especially in an exaggerated and self-indulgent way.
2. **Concise Meaning:** emotional; nostalgic; overly emotional
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The old photographs made her feel **sentimental**.
    *  He is a **sentimental** person who cries easily at movies.
4. **Opposite Words:** unsentimental, pragmatic
5. **GRE Synonyms:** mawkish, nostalgic

**25. squander**
1. **Definition:** Waste (something, especially money or time) in a reckless and foolish manner.
2. **Concise Meaning:** waste foolishly; spend recklessly
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Don't **squander** your opportunities on trivial pursuits.
    *  He **squandered** his inheritance on gambling.
4. **Opposite Words:** conserve, save
5. **GRE Synonyms:** dissipate, fritter

**26. swindle**
1. **Definition:** Use deception to deprive someone of money or possessions.
2. **Concise Meaning:** cheat; defraud; deceive for money
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He was **swindled** out of his life savings by a con artist.
    *  The fake charity tried to **swindle** people.
4. **Opposite Words:** recompense, compensate
5. **GRE Synonyms:** defraud, bilk

**27. tangible**
1. **Definition:** Perceptible by touch.
2. **Concise Meaning:** real; touchable; concrete
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The tension in the room was almost **tangible**.
    *  Success became **tangible** after years of hard work.
4. **Opposite Words:** intangible, abstract
5. **GRE Synonyms:** palpable, corporeal

**28. turpitude**
1. **Definition:** Depravity; wickedness.
2. **Concise Meaning:** wickedness; moral depravity
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The judge condemned his moral **turpitude**.
    *  His acts of **turpitude** shocked the community.
4. **Opposite Words:** virtue, righteousness
5. **GRE Synonyms:** depravity, baseness

**29. unalloyed**
1. **Definition:** (chiefly of emotions) complete and unreserved.
2. **Concise Meaning:** pure; unmixed; complete
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The child showed **unalloyed** joy at receiving the gift.
    *  It was a moment of **unalloyed** happiness.
4. **Opposite Words:** adulterated, mixed
5. **GRE Synonyms:** pure, unqualified

**30. undercut(1)**
1. **Definition:** Offer goods or services at a lower price than (a competitor).
2. **Concise Meaning:** sell cheaper; price lower
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The new store **undercut** its rivals to gain market share.
    *  They **undercut** competitors by offering discounts.
4. **Opposite Words:** overcharge, inflate
5. **GRE Synonyms:** undersell, cheapen

**31. undercut(2)**
1. **Definition:** Undermine the power or effectiveness of (something).
2. **Concise Meaning:** weaken; undermine; sabotage
3. **Sentences:**  *  His criticism **undercut** her confidence.
    *  The scandal **undercut** the company's reputation.
4. **Opposite Words:** bolster, reinforce
5. **GRE Synonyms:** impair, sabotage

**32. wheedle**
1. **Definition:** Use flattery or coaxing to persuade someone to do something or give one something.
2. **Concise Meaning:** coax; flatter; persuade gently
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She **wheedled** her way into getting backstage passes.
    *  He tried to **wheedle** information out of her.
4. **Opposite Words:** demand, bully
5. **GRE Synonyms:** cajole, coax

**33. xenophobic**
1. **Definition:** Having or showing a dislike of or prejudice against people from other countries.
2. **Concise Meaning:** fear of foreigners; prejudiced
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **xenophobic** remarks were widely condemned.
    *  The country's policies were criticized as **xenophobic**.
4. **Opposite Words:** cosmopolitan, welcoming
5. **GRE Synonyms:** jingoistic, chauvinistic

      "intangible",
      "abstract"
    ],
    "synonyms": [
      "palpable",
      "corporeal"
    ]
  },
  {
    "word": "turpitude",
    "definition": "Depravity; wickedness.",
    "concise_meaning": "wickedness; moral depravity",
    "sentences": [
      "The judge condemned his moral **turpitude**.",
      "His acts of **turpitude** shocked the community."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "virtue",
      "righteousness"
    ],
    "synonyms": [
      "depravity",
      "baseness"
    ]
  },
  {
    "word": "unalloyed",
    "definition": "(chiefly of emotions) complete and unreserved.",
    "concise_meaning": "pure; unmixed; complete",
    "sentences": [
      "The child showed **unalloyed** joy at receiving the gift.",
      "It was a moment of **unalloyed** happiness."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "adulterated",
      "mixed"
    ],
    "synonyms": [
      "pure",
      "unqualified"
    ]
  },
  {
    "word": "undercut(1)",

    "concise_meaning": "sell cheaper; price lower",

      "The new store **undercut** its rivals to gain market share.",
      "They **undercut** competitors by offering discounts."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "overcharge",
      "inflate"
    ],
    "synonyms": [
      "undersell",
      "cheapen"
    ]
  },
  {
    "word": "undercut(2)",
    "definition": "Undermine the power or effectiveness of (something).",
    "concise_meaning": "weaken; undermine; sabotage",
    "sentences": [
      "His criticism **undercut** her confidence.",
      "The scandal **undercut** the company's reputation."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "bolster",
      "reinforce"

      "impair",

  {
    "word": "wheedle",
    "definition": "Use flattery or coaxing to persuade someone to do something or give one something.",
    "concise_meaning": "coax; flatter; persuade gently",
    "sentences": [
      "She **wheedled** her way into getting backstage passes.",
      "He tried to **wheedle** information out of her."

      "cajole",

  {
    "word": "xenophobic",
    "definition": "Having or showing a dislike of or prejudice against people from other countries.",
    "concise_meaning": "fear of foreigners; prejudiced",
    "sentences": [
      "His **xenophobic** remarks were widely condemned.",
      "The country's policies were criticized as **xenophobic**."
    ],

      "cosmopolitan",
      "welcoming"
    ],
    "synonyms": [
      "jingoistic",
      "chauvinistic"

# 28
**1. abeyance**
1. **Definition:**  A state of temporary disuse or suspension.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Temporary suspension or inactivity
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The project was held in **abeyance** pending further funding.
    *  Legal proceedings were in **abeyance** while negotiations continued.
4. **Opposite Words:**  continuation, operation
5. **GRE Synonyms:** dormancy, quiescence

**2. abstract (1)**
1. **Definition:**  Existing in thought or as an idea but not having a physical or concrete existence.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Existing as idea, not concrete
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Justice is an **abstract** concept, difficult to define precisely.
    *  He dealt with **abstract** ideas rather than practical matters.
4. **Opposite Words:** concrete, tangible
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  conceptual, theoretical

**3. abstract (2)**
1. **Definition:**  Summarize (a text, document, or speech).
2. **Concise Meaning:** Summarize or extract main points
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She **abstracted** the key findings from the lengthy report.
    *  Can you **abstract** the main points of this article for me?
4. **Opposite Words:**  expand, elaborate
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  condense, epitomize

**4. affront**
1. **Definition:**  An action or remark that causes outrage or offence.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Deliberate insult or offense
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His rude comment was a direct **affront** to her dignity.
    *  She took his criticism as a personal **affront**.
4. **Opposite Words:**  compliment, respect
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  insult, indignity

**5. agitate**
1. **Definition:**  Make (someone) troubled or nervous.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  To disturb or make anxious
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Bad news can **agitate** people and cause worry.
    *  The rumors **agitated** the community and created unrest.
4. **Opposite Words:**  calm, soothe
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  disquiet, perturb

**6. august**
1. **Definition:**  Respected and impressive.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Dignified and highly respected
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **august** ceremony was attended by dignitaries.
    *  He comes from an **august** lineage of scholars.
4. **Opposite Words:**  undignified, common
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  majestic, venerable

**7. burnish**
1. **Definition:**  Polish (something, especially metal) by rubbing.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  To polish and make shiny
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She used polish to **burnish** the silver cutlery.
    *  He **burnished** his shoes until they gleamed.
4. **Opposite Words:**  dull, tarnish
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  polish, shine

**8. coy**
1. **Definition:**  Making a pretence of shyness or modesty that is intended to be alluring.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Pretending shyness to be alluring
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She gave him a **coy** smile from behind her fan.
    *  He found her **coy** demeanor quite charming.
4. **Opposite Words:**  brazen, forward
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  demure, bashful

**9. deprecate**
1. **Definition:**  Express disapproval of.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  To disapprove or criticize
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She **deprecated** his reckless driving habits.
    *  The committee **deprecated** the proposed budget cuts.
4. **Opposite Words:**  approve, commend
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  disparage, belittle

**10. disdain**
1. **Definition:**  The feeling that someone or something is unworthy of one's consideration or respect; contempt.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Contempt; feeling of superiority
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She looked at him with **disdain** and turned away.
    *  He spoke of the new policy with open **disdain**.
4. **Opposite Words:**  respect, admiration
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  scorn, contempt

**11. disperse**
1. **Definition:**  Distribute or spread over a wide area.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  To scatter or spread out
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The crowd began to **disperse** after the concert ended.
    *  The seeds are **dispersed** by the wind.
4. **Opposite Words:**  gather, assemble
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  scatter, dissipate

**12. distend**
1. **Definition:**  Swell or cause to swell by pressure from inside.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  To swell or expand outwards
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her stomach began to **distend** after the large meal.
    *  The balloon **distended** as it was filled with air.
4. **Opposite Words:**  contract, deflate
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  dilate, inflate

**13. endemic**
1. **Definition:**  (Of a disease or condition) regularly found among particular people or in a certain area.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Native or restricted to area
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Malaria is **endemic** to many tropical regions.
    *  Poverty is an **endemic** problem in some communities.
4. **Opposite Words:**  pandemic, foreign
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  native, indigenous

**14. enmity**
1. **Definition:**  The state or feeling of being actively opposed or hostile to someone or something.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Deep-seated hatred or hostility
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Decades of **enmity** existed between the two families.
    *  Political **enmity** can divide nations and communities.
4. **Opposite Words:**  friendship, amity
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  hostility, animosity

**15. gauche**
1. **Definition:**  Lacking ease or grace; unsophisticated and socially awkward.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Awkward and socially inept
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **gauche** manners made him feel out of place at the formal dinner.
    *  It was considered **gauche** to talk about money in polite society.
4. **Opposite Words:**  graceful, sophisticated
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  clumsy, inept

**16. hysterical**
1. **Definition:**  Affected by or deriving from wildly uncontrolled emotion.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Uncontrolled emotion or excitement
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She became **hysterical** after hearing the shocking news.
    *  The crowd was **hysterical** with excitement at the concert.
4. **Opposite Words:**  calm, composed
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  frenzied, overwrought

**17. impudent**
1. **Definition:**  Not showing due respect for another person; impertinent.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Disrespectful and bold; rude
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The student was punished for his **impudent** behavior towards the teacher.
    *  His **impudent** remark shocked everyone in the room.
4. **Opposite Words:**  respectful, polite
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  insolent, brazen

**18. inchoate**
1. **Definition:**  Just begun and so not fully formed or developed; rudimentary.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Not fully formed or developed
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The idea was still **inchoate** and needed more refinement.
    *  His feelings were **inchoate**, a mixture of confusion and excitement.
4. **Opposite Words:**  developed, mature
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  rudimentary, nascent

**19. penchant**
1. **Definition:**  A habitual inclination or tendency to do something.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Strong liking or inclination
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He has a **penchant** for spicy food.
    *  She shows a **penchant** for classical music.
4. **Opposite Words:**  dislike, aversion
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  predilection, affinity

**20. quandary**
1. **Definition:**  A state of perplexity or uncertainty over what to do in a difficult situation.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  State of uncertainty or dilemma
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He was in a **quandary** about which job offer to accept.
    *  The ethical **quandary** presented a difficult choice.
4. **Opposite Words:**  certainty, resolution
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  dilemma, predicament

**21. quarantine**
1. **Definition:**  A state, period, or place of isolation in which people or animals that have arrived from elsewhere or been exposed to infectious or contagious disease are placed.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Isolation to prevent disease spread
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The ship was placed in **quarantine** due to a suspected outbreak.
    *  They had to **quarantine** the infected animals to stop the epidemic.
4. **Opposite Words:**  release, socialize
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  isolation, seclusion

**22. quash**
1. **Definition:**  Reject as invalid, especially by legal procedure.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  To suppress or invalidate
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The court **quashed** the lower court's decision.
    *  Police quickly **quashed** the riot before it escalated.
4. **Opposite Words:**  uphold, instigate
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  suppress, annul

**23. quibble**
1. **Definition:**  Argue or raise objections about a trivial matter.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Argue over minor details
3. **Sentences:**
    *  They **quibbled** over the exact wording of the contract.
    *  Don't **quibble** about small things; focus on the main issue.
4. **Opposite Words:**  agree, concur
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  cavil, bicker

**24. ravage**
1. **Definition:**  Cause severe and extensive damage to.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  To severely damage or destroy
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The hurricane **ravaged** the coastal town.
    *  War can **ravage** a country and its infrastructure.
4. **Opposite Words:**  restore, build
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  devastate, despoil

**25. recant**
1. **Definition:**  Say that one no longer holds an opinion or belief, especially one considered heretical.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Withdraw or disavow belief
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He **recanted** his earlier statement after facing criticism.
    *  Under pressure, she **recanted** her confession.
4. **Opposite Words:**  affirm, assert
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  retract, disavow

**26. redoubtable**
1. **Definition:**  (Of a person) formidable, especially as an opponent.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Formidable and commanding respect
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He was a **redoubtable** debater, known for his sharp wit.
    *  The general was a **redoubtable** figure in military history.
4. **Opposite Words:**  weak, timid
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  formidable, intimidating

**27. retiring**
1. **Definition:**  Shy and fond of being on one's own.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Shy and avoids company
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She is a **retiring** person who prefers quiet evenings at home.
    *  His **retiring** nature made him uncomfortable in large crowds.
4. **Opposite Words:**  outgoing, gregarious
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  introverted, diffident

**28. shrill**
1. **Definition:**  (Of a voice or sound) high-pitched and piercing.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  High-pitched and piercing sound
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **shrill** whistle startled everyone in the park.
    *  Her voice became **shrill** with anger.
4. **Opposite Words:**  deep, low
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  piercing, strident

**29. sophistry**
1. **Definition:**  The use of clever but false arguments, especially with the intention of deceiving.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Deceptive and false reasoning
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His argument was full of **sophistry** and lacked real substance.
    *  Don't be fooled by his **sophistry**; his claims are baseless.
4. **Opposite Words:**  truth, honesty
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  fallacy, deception

**30. substantiate**
1. **Definition:**  Provide evidence to support or prove the truth of.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  To prove with evidence
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The scientist could not **substantiate** his hypothesis with data.
    *  Witness testimony helped **substantiate** the victim's account.
4. **Opposite Words:**  disprove, invalidate
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  verify, validate

**31. wily**
1. **Definition:**  Skilled at gaining an advantage, especially deceitfully.
2. **Concise Meaning:**  Cunning and deceitful; sly
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **wily** fox outsmarted the hunters.
    *  He was known for his **wily** business tactics.
4. **Opposite Words:**  honest, straightforward
5. **GRE Synonyms:**  cunning, shrewd

      "They **quibbled** over the exact wording of the contract.",
      "Don't **quibble** about small things; focus on the main issue."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "agree",
      "concur"
    ],
    "gre_synonyms": [
      "cavil",
      "bicker"
    ]
  },
  "ravage": {
    "definition": "Cause severe and extensive damage to.",
    "concise_meaning": "To severely damage or destroy",
    "sentences": [
      "The hurricane **ravaged** the coastal town.",
      "War can **ravage** a country and its infrastructure."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "restore",
      "build"
    ],
    "gre_synonyms": [
      "devastate",
      "despoil"
    ]
  },
  "recant": {
    "definition": "Say that one no longer holds an opinion or belief, especially one considered heretical.",
    "concise_meaning": "Withdraw or disavow belief",
    "sentences": [
      "He **recanted** his earlier statement after facing criticism.",
      "Under pressure, she **recanted** her confession."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "affirm",
      "assert"
    ],
    "gre_synonyms": [
      "retract",
      "disavow"
    ]
  },
  "redoubtable": {
    "definition": "(Of a person) formidable, especially as an opponent.",
    "concise_meaning": "Formidable and commanding respect",
    "sentences": [
      "He was a **redoubtable** debater, known for his sharp wit.",
      "The general was a **redoubtable** figure in military history."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "weak",
      "timid"
    ],
    "gre_synonyms": [
      "formidable",
      "intimidating"
    ]
  },
  "retiring": {
    "definition": "Shy and fond of being on one's own.",
    "concise_meaning": "Shy and avoids company",
    "sentences": [
      "She is a **retiring** person who prefers quiet evenings at home.",
      "His **retiring** nature made him uncomfortable in large crowds."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "outgoing",
      "gregarious"
    ],
    "gre_synonyms": [
      "introverted",
      "diffident"
    ]
  },
  "shrill": {
    "definition": "(Of a voice or sound) high-pitched and piercing.",
    "concise_meaning": "High-pitched and piercing sound",
    "sentences": [
      "The **shrill** whistle startled everyone in the park.",
      "Her voice became **shrill** with anger."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "deep",
      "low"
    ],
    "gre_synonyms": [
      "piercing",
      "strident"
    ]
  },
  "sophistry": {
    "definition": "The use of clever but false arguments, especially with the intention of deceiving.",
    "concise_meaning": "Deceptive and false reasoning",
    "sentences": [
      "His argument was full of **sophistry** and lacked real substance.",
      "Don't be fooled by his **sophistry**; his claims are baseless."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "truth",
      "honesty"
    ],
    "gre_synonyms": [
      "fallacy",
      "deception"
    ]
  },
  "substantiate": {
    "definition": "Provide evidence to support or prove the truth of.",
    "concise_meaning": "To prove with evidence",
    "sentences": [
      "The scientist could not **substantiate** his hypothesis with data.",
      "Witness testimony helped **substantiate** the victim's account."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "disprove",
      "invalidate"
    ],
    "gre_synonyms": [
      "verify",
      "validate"
    ]
  },
  "wily": {
    "definition": "Skilled at gaining an advantage, especially deceitfully.",
    "concise_meaning": "Cunning and deceitful; sly",
    "sentences": [
      "The **wily** fox outsmarted the hunters.",
      "He was known for his **wily** business tactics."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "honest",
      "straightforward"
    ],
    "gre_synonyms": [
      "cunning",
      "shrewd"
    ]
  }
}
```


# 29
**1. abscond**
1. **Definition:** Leave hurriedly and secretly, typically to avoid detection of or arrest for an unlawful action such as theft.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Secretly run away to escape
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The treasurer **absconded** with the charity's funds, leaving everyone in shock.
    *  To avoid prosecution, the suspect **absconded** to a country with no extradition treaty.
4. **Opposite Words:** appear, remain
5. **GRE Synonyms:** decamp, flee

**2. apogee**
1. **Definition:** The highest point in the development of something; a climax or culmination.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Highest point; culmination
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Winning the championship was the **apogee** of his basketball career.
    *  The Roman Empire reached its **apogee** in the second century AD.
4. **Opposite Words:** nadir, perigee
5. **GRE Synonyms:** apex, zenith

**3. aspersion**
1. **Definition:** An attack on the reputation or integrity of someone or something.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Damaging or false accusation
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The politician cast **aspersions** on his opponent's character during the debate.
    *  Despite the **aspersions** cast upon her, she maintained her dignity and composure.
4. **Opposite Words:** praise, compliment
5. **GRE Synonyms:** slander, defamation

**4. bawdy**
1. **Definition:** Dealing with sexual matters in a comical way; humorously indecent.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Humorously indecent or sexual
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The play was known for its **bawdy** humor and suggestive jokes.
    *  His **bawdy** remarks made some guests uncomfortable at the dinner party.
4. **Opposite Words:** decent, moral
5. **GRE Synonyms:** ribald, risque

**5. chagrin**
1. **Definition:** Annoyance or distress at having failed or been humiliated.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Embarrassment from failure
3. **Sentences:**
    *  To his **chagrin**, he realized he had forgotten his wallet at home.
    *  She felt a deep sense of **chagrin** after losing the singing competition.
4. **Opposite Words:** delight, elation
5. **GRE Synonyms:** mortification, discomfiture

**6. collude**
1. **Definition:** Cooperate in a secret or unlawful way in order to deceive or gain an advantage over others.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Secretly cooperate for deceit
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The companies were accused of **colluding** to fix prices and stifle competition.
    *  It was suspected that some officials **colluded** with the criminals to help them escape.
4. **Opposite Words:** disagree, oppose
5. **GRE Synonyms:** conspire, connive

**7. commiserate**
1. **Definition:** Express or feel sympathy or pity; sympathize.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Express sympathy; sympathize
3. **Sentences:**
    *  I **commiserated** with her after she failed her driving test.
    *  The team members **commiserated** over their unexpected loss.
4. **Opposite Words:** disregard, ignore
5. **GRE Synonyms:** condole, empathize

**8. conflagration**
1. **Definition:** An extensive fire which destroys a great deal of land or property.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Large destructive fire
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **conflagration** engulfed the entire forest, leaving behind only ashes.
    *  Firefighters struggled to contain the **conflagration** that broke out in the city center.
4. **Opposite Words:** drizzle, sprinkle
5. **GRE Synonyms:** inferno, blaze

**9. contretemps**
1. **Definition:** A minor dispute or disagreement; an unexpected or unfortunate occurrence.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Minor awkward disagreement
3. **Sentences:**
    *  A slight **contretemps** arose when they disagreed on the restaurant choice.
    *  The wedding faced a minor **contretemps** when the cake delivery was late.
4. **Opposite Words:** agreement, harmony
5. **GRE Synonyms:** squabble, mishap

**10. conviction**
1. **Definition:** A firmly held belief or opinion.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Firmly held belief
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She spoke with **conviction** about the importance of environmental protection.
    *  His strong **conviction** in justice motivated him to become a lawyer.
4. **Opposite Words:** doubt, uncertainty
5. **GRE Synonyms:** certitude, faith

**11. croon**
1. **Definition:** Hum or sing in a soft, low voice, especially in a sentimental manner.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Sing softly and sentimentally
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He **crooned** a lullaby to soothe the baby to sleep.
    *  The singer **crooned** romantic ballads to the captivated audience.
4. **Opposite Words:** yell, shout
5. **GRE Synonyms:** warble, hum

**12. depose**
1. **Definition:** Remove from office suddenly and forcefully.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Remove from power forcefully
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The military coup **deposed** the dictator and established a new government.
    *  The shareholders voted to **depose** the CEO due to poor performance.
4. **Opposite Words:** enthrone, instate
5. **GRE Synonyms:** oust, unseat

**13. detente**
1. **Definition:** The easing of hostility or strained relations, especially between countries.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Easing of strained relations
3. **Sentences:**
    *  A period of **detente** began between the two nations after years of conflict.
    *  Diplomacy aimed to achieve **detente** and prevent further escalation of tensions.
4. **Opposite Words:** hostility, conflict
5. **GRE Synonyms:** reconciliation, rapprochement

**14. dowdy**
1. **Definition:** Unfashionable and dull in appearance (typically used of a woman or of clothes).
2. **Concise Meaning:** Unfashionable and dull appearance
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She felt **dowdy** in her old clothes compared to the stylish women around her.
    *  The office had a **dowdy** atmosphere with its outdated furniture and dim lighting.
4. **Opposite Words:** stylish, fashionable
5. **GRE Synonyms:** frumpy, drab

**15. echelon**
1. **Definition:** A level or rank in an organization, a profession, or society.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Level or rank in hierarchy
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He rose through the **echelons** of the company to become a senior executive.
    *  The military structure is organized in clear **echelons** of command.
4. **Opposite Words:** base, bottom
5. **GRE Synonyms:** rank, grade

**16. ennui**
1. **Definition:** A feeling of listlessness and dissatisfaction arising from a lack of occupation or excitement.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Boredom and dissatisfaction
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She suffered from **ennui** during the long, monotonous summer vacation.
    *  The wealthy heir was plagued by **ennui** despite having every material comfort.
4. **Opposite Words:** excitement, enthusiasm
5. **GRE Synonyms:** tedium, languor

**17. expatiate**
1. **Definition:** Speak or write at length or in detail.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Speak or write at length
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The professor **expatiated** on the intricacies of quantum physics for hours.
    *  She **expatiated** on her travel experiences, captivating the audience.
4. **Opposite Words:** condense, abridge
5. **GRE Synonyms:** elaborate, dilate

**18. fraught**
1. **Definition:** (of a situation or course of action) filled with or destined to cause anxiety or distress.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Filled with anxiety or danger
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The negotiation process was **fraught** with tension and disagreements.
    *  Their journey across the desert was **fraught** with peril and uncertainty.
4. **Opposite Words:** peaceful, calm
5. **GRE Synonyms:** perilous, anxious

**19. fulcrum**
1. **Definition:** The point on which a lever rests or is supported and on which it pivots.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Pivot point of a lever
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The rock served as a **fulcrum** for the makeshift lever.
    *  Understanding the **fulcrum** is essential for using leverage effectively.
4. **Opposite Words:** weight, resistance
5. **GRE Synonyms:** pivot, hinge

**20. imbroglio**
1. **Definition:** An extremely confused, complicated, or embarrassing situation.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Confused or embarrassing situation
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The political scandal plunged the government into a deep **imbroglio**.
    *  Their personal relationship became an **imbroglio** of misunderstandings and accusations.
4. **Opposite Words:** order, clarity
5. **GRE Synonyms:** entanglement, quandary

**21. jocund**
1. **Definition:** Cheerful and lighthearted.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Cheerful and lighthearted
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **jocund** atmosphere of the party was infectious and joyous.
    *  His **jocund** nature made him a pleasure to be around.
4. **Opposite Words:** morose, gloomy
5. **GRE Synonyms:** blithe, jovial

**22. languish (1)**
1. **Definition:** (of a person or other living thing) lose or lack vitality; grow weak or feeble.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Become weak; lose vitality
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The plants **languished** in the drought, lacking water and sunlight.
    *  After months in captivity, the prisoner began to **languish**.
4. **Opposite Words:** thrive, flourish
5. **GRE Synonyms:** weaken, deteriorate

**23. languish (2)**
1. **Definition:** Fail to make progress or be successful.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Fail to progress or succeed
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her career **languished** despite her hard work and dedication.
    *  The peace talks **languished** due to lack of agreement from both sides.
4. **Opposite Words:** advance, prosper
5. **GRE Synonyms:** stagnate, decline

**24. nadir**
1. **Definition:** The lowest point in the fortunes of a person or organization.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Lowest point; rock bottom
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The company reached its **nadir** during the financial crisis.
    *  His personal life hit its **nadir** after losing his job and home.
4. **Opposite Words:** apogee, zenith
5. **GRE Synonyms:** bottom, depth

**25. nimble**
1. **Definition:** Quick and light in movement or action; agile.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Quick and agile movement
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The dancer was **nimble** on her feet, gliding across the stage with ease.
    *  His **nimble** fingers quickly typed out the email.
4. **Opposite Words:** clumsy, awkward
5. **GRE Synonyms:** adroit, deft

**26. ominous**
1. **Definition:** Giving the impression that something bad or unpleasant is going to happen; threatening.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Threatening; predicting bad events
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The dark clouds gathering overhead looked **ominous**.
    *  His **ominous** words filled her with a sense of foreboding.
4. **Opposite Words:** auspicious, promising
5. **GRE Synonyms:** foreboding, portentous

**27. outlandish**
1. **Definition:** Looking or sounding bizarre or unfamiliar; foreign.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Bizarre; strange; unconventional
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She wore an **outlandish** outfit to the party, attracting a lot of attention.
    *  His ideas were considered **outlandish** by the conservative committee.
4. **Opposite Words:** ordinary, conventional
5. **GRE Synonyms:** eccentric, bizarre

**28. propitious**
1. **Definition:** Giving or indicating a good chance of success; favourable.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Favorable; good chance of success
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The weather was **propitious** for sailing, with calm seas and a gentle breeze.
    *  It was a **propitious** time to invest in the stock market.
4. **Opposite Words:** unfavorable, inauspicious
5. **GRE Synonyms:** auspicious, fortunate

**29. prurient**
1. **Definition:** Having or encouraging an excessive interest in sexual matters, especially the sexual activity of others.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Excessively interested in sex
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The tabloid newspaper was criticized for its **prurient** coverage of celebrity scandals.
    *  His **prurient** curiosity about his neighbor's private life was inappropriate.
4. **Opposite Words:** modest, decent
5. **GRE Synonyms:** lascivious, lewd

**30. sadistic**
1. **Definition:** Deriving pleasure from inflicting pain, suffering, or humiliation on others.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Pleasure from inflicting pain
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The bully displayed **sadistic** tendencies by tormenting the smaller children.
    *  The villain in the movie was portrayed as a **sadistic** and cruel character.
4. **Opposite Words:** compassionate, kind
5. **GRE Synonyms:** cruel, brutal

**31. zenith**
1. **Definition:** The time at which something is most powerful or successful.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Peak; highest point of success
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The band reached their **zenith** of popularity in the late 1990s.
    *  Her career reached its **zenith** when she won the Nobel Prize.
4. **Opposite Words:** nadir, bottom
5. **GRE Synonyms:** apex, apogee

    "sentences": [
      "The rock served as a **fulcrum** for the makeshift lever.",
      "Understanding the **fulcrum** is essential for using leverage effectively."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [
      "weight",
      "resistance"
    ],
    "synonyms": [
      "pivot",
      "hinge"
    ]

  {

    ],

  },
  {

    ],
    "opposite_words": [

    ],

      "blithe",

  {

    "definition": "(of a person or other living thing) lose or lack vitality; grow weak or feeble.",

    ],

  {
    "word(2)": "languish",

    "sentences": [
      "Her career **languished** despite her hard work and dedication.",
      "The peace talks **languished** due to lack of agreement from both sides."
    ],
    "opposite_words": [

      "stagnate",

      "The company reached its **nadir** during the financial crisis.",
      "His personal life hit its **nadir** after losing his job and home."

    "concise_meaning": "Threatening; predicting bad events",

      "The dark clouds gathering overhead looked **ominous**.",

# 30
**1. aberrant**
1. **Definition:** Departing from an accepted standard.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Deviating from the norm
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her **aberrant** behavior at the party raised eyebrows.
    *  The **aberrant** weather patterns this year are a cause for concern.
4. **Opposite Words:** normal, typical
5. **GRE Synonyms:** anomalous, deviant

**2. abide**
1. **Definition:** Accept or act in accordance with (a rule, decision, or recommendation).
2. **Concise Meaning:** To comply with or obey
3. **Sentences:**
    *  You must **abide** by the rules of the competition.
    *  Citizens should **abide** by the laws of their country.
4. **Opposite Words:** defy, resist
5. **GRE Synonyms:** adhere, conform

**3. bravado**
1. **Definition:** A bold manner or a show of boldness intended to impress or intimidate.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Showy boldness or false courage
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **bravado** masked his underlying fear.
    *  The bully's **bravado** quickly disappeared when challenged.
4. **Opposite Words:** timidity, fearfulness
5. **GRE Synonyms:** swagger, bluster

**4. callow**
1. **Definition:** Inexperienced and immature.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Immature and lacking experience
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **callow** youth made a series of naive mistakes.
    *  His **callow** remarks revealed his lack of understanding.
4. **Opposite Words:** mature, experienced
5. **GRE Synonyms:** juvenile, green

**5. capitulate**
1. **Definition:** Cease to resist an opponent or an unwelcome demand; surrender.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To surrender or give in
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The army decided to **capitulate** after heavy losses.
    *  She refused to **capitulate** to his unreasonable demands.
4. **Opposite Words:** resist, withstand
5. **GRE Synonyms:** succumb, yield

**6. cogitate**
1. **Definition:** Think deeply about something; meditate or reflect.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To think deeply or ponder
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He needed time to **cogitate** on the complex problem.
    *  She would often **cogitate** about the meaning of life.
4. **Opposite Words:** disregard, ignore
5. **GRE Synonyms:** contemplate, ruminate

**7. deportment**
1. **Definition:** A person's behavior or manners.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Behavior or manner of conduct
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Her elegant **deportment** impressed everyone at the ball.
    *  Good **deportment** is expected in formal settings.
4. **Opposite Words:** impropriety, rudeness
5. **GRE Synonyms:** demeanor, conduct

**8. extemporize**
1. **Definition:** Compose, perform, or produce something such as music or a speech without preparation; improvise.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To improvise or speak spontaneously
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He had to **extemporize** his speech when his notes were lost.
    *  The jazz musician could **extemporize** beautiful melodies.
4. **Opposite Words:** plan, prepare
5. **GRE Synonyms:** improvise, ad-lib

**9. factious**
1. **Definition:** Relating to or characterized by faction; dissentious.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Causing disagreement or discord
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **factious** committee was unable to reach a consensus.
    *  **Factious** disputes threatened to split the organization.
4. **Opposite Words:** harmonious, unified
5. **GRE Synonyms:** divisive, schismatic

**10. fallow(1)**
1. **Definition:** (of farmland) plowed and harrowed but left unsown for a period in order to restore its fertility as part of a crop rotation or to avoid surplus production.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Uncultivated land, resting soil
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The farmer left the field **fallow** to replenish nutrients.
    *  **Fallow** land is often used in crop rotation.
4. **Opposite Words:** cultivated, planted
5. **GRE Synonyms:** unseeded, dormant

**11. fallow(2)**
1. **Definition:** (of a period of time) inactive.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Inactive, unproductive period
3. **Sentences:**
    *  After years of success, his career entered a **fallow** period.
    *  Creativity can sometimes lie **fallow** before blossoming again.
4. **Opposite Words:** productive, active
5. **GRE Synonyms:** dormant, unproductive

**12. feint**
1. **Definition:** A deceptive or pretended blow, thrust, or other movement, especially in boxing or fencing.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Deceptive movement, fake attack
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The boxer used a **feint** to confuse his opponent.
    *  Her smile was just a **feint** to hide her true feelings.
4. **Opposite Words:** honesty, directness
5. **GRE Synonyms:** ruse, bluff

**13. flagrant**
1. **Definition:** (of something considered wrong or immoral) conspicuously or obviously offensive.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Obviously offensive or outrageous
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **flagrant** disregard for the rules led to his dismissal.
    *  It was a **flagrant** violation of international law.
4. **Opposite Words:** inconspicuous, minor
5. **GRE Synonyms:** blatant, egregious

**14. gratuitous**
1. **Definition:** Uncalled for; lacking good reason; unwarranted.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Unnecessary and uncalled for
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The movie contained **gratuitous** violence that added nothing to the plot.
    *  Her insult was completely **gratuitous** and hurtful.
4. **Opposite Words:** warranted, necessary
5. **GRE Synonyms:** unwarranted, superfluous

**15. grovel**
1. **Definition:** Act obsequiously in order to obtain someone's forgiveness or favor.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To beg or act subserviently
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He had to **grovel** before his boss to keep his job.
    *  She refused to **grovel** for forgiveness she didn't believe she needed.
4. **Opposite Words:** disdain, scorn
5. **GRE Synonyms:** fawn, kowtow

**16. indecorous**
1. **Definition:** Not in keeping with good taste and propriety; improper.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Improper, lacking good taste
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **indecorous** behavior at the funeral shocked everyone.
    *  Wearing jeans to a wedding is considered **indecorous**.
4. **Opposite Words:** proper, decorous
5. **GRE Synonyms:** unseemly, inappropriate

**17. intrigue(1)**
1. **Definition:** Arouse one's curiosity or interest.
2. **Concise Meaning:** To fascinate or interest greatly
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The mysterious story **intrigued** her from the beginning.
    *  The ancient artifact **intrigued** the archaeologists.
4. **Opposite Words:** bore, disinterest
5. **GRE Synonyms:** captivate, fascinate

**18. intrigue(2)**
1. **Definition:** Secret or cunning schemes; plots.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Secret plot or scheme
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Political **intrigues** were common in the royal court.
    *  He was caught up in a web of dangerous **intrigues**.
4. **Opposite Words:** honesty, openness
5. **GRE Synonyms:** conspiracy, machination

**19. nominal(1)**
1. **Definition:** (of a role or status) existing in name only.
2. **Concise Meaning:** In name only, not real
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He was the **nominal** head of the department, but had no real power.
    *  The fee was **nominal**, just a symbolic amount.
4. **Opposite Words:** real, actual
5. **GRE Synonyms:** titular, ostensible

**20. nominal(2)**
1. **Definition:** (of a price or charge) very small; far below the actual value or cost.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Very small, insignificant value
3. **Sentences:**
    *  They charged a **nominal** fee for entrance to the museum.
    *  The rent was **nominal** considering the size of the apartment.
4. **Opposite Words:** substantial, significant
5. **GRE Synonyms:** negligible, trifling

**21. obdurate**
1. **Definition:** Stubbornly refusing to change one's opinion or course of action.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Stubborn and unyielding, inflexible
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He was **obdurate** in his refusal to apologize.
    *  Despite pleas, her **obdurate** stance remained unchanged.
4. **Opposite Words:** compliant, flexible
5. **GRE Synonyms:** intransigent, adamant

**22. obstreperous**
1. **Definition:** Noisy and difficult to control.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Noisy, unruly, and difficult to control
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **obstreperous** crowd disrupted the meeting.
    *  The teacher struggled to manage the **obstreperous** students.
4. **Opposite Words:** quiet, docile
5. **GRE Synonyms:** clamorous, vociferous

**23. odious**
1. **Definition:** Extremely unpleasant; repulsive.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Repulsive, hateful, disgusting
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The smell of rotten eggs is truly **odious**.
    *  He found the task of cleaning the bathroom **odious**.
4. **Opposite Words:** pleasant, delightful
5. **GRE Synonyms:** abhorrent, repugnant

**24. plucky**
1. **Definition:** Having or showing determined courage in the face of difficulties.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Courageous and brave spirited
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **plucky** child faced her fears with bravery.
    *  Despite the odds, they showed a **plucky** determination to succeed.
4. **Opposite Words:** cowardly, timid
5. **GRE Synonyms:** valiant, intrepid

**25. precocious**
1. **Definition:** Having developed certain abilities or proclivities at an earlier age than usual.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Early developed abilities or skills
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The **precocious** child was reading novels at age five.
    *  Her **precocious** musical talent was evident from a young age.
4. **Opposite Words:** backward, slow
5. **GRE Synonyms:** gifted, advanced

**26. remuneration**
1. **Definition:** Money paid for work or a service.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Payment for work or service
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He received fair **remuneration** for his hard work.
    *  The job offered excellent **remuneration** and benefits.
4. **Opposite Words:** debt, loss
5. **GRE Synonyms:** compensation, recompense

**27. slovenly(1)**
1. **Definition:** (especially of a person or their appearance) careless, excessively casual, or untidy.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Untidy, careless in appearance
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **slovenly** appearance at the interview hurt his chances.
    *  She was known for her **slovenly** habits around the house.
4. **Opposite Words:** neat, tidy
5. **GRE Synonyms:** unkempt, disheveled

**28. slovenly(2)**
1. **Definition:** (especially of work) done in a careless, slipshod way.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Careless, slipshod work
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The report was full of **slovenly** errors and typos.
    *  He did a **slovenly** job of painting the fence.
4. **Opposite Words:** meticulous, careful
5. **GRE Synonyms:** slipshod, slapdash

**29. soliloquy**
1. **Definition:** An act of speaking one's thoughts aloud when by oneself or regardless of any hearers, especially by a character in a play.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Speaking thoughts aloud to oneself
3. **Sentences:**
    *  Hamlet's famous **soliloquy** begins "To be or not to be".
    *  The play included a long **soliloquy** revealing the character's inner turmoil.
4. **Opposite Words:** dialogue, conversation
5. **GRE Synonyms:** monologue, aside

**30. spurn**
1. **Definition:** Reject with disdain or contempt.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Reject with contempt or disdain
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She **spurned** his offer of help, refusing to accept it.
    *  He **spurned** their advances, showing no interest in joining.
4. **Opposite Words:** accept, welcome
5. **GRE Synonyms:** rebuff, disdain

**31. stolid**
1. **Definition:** (of a person) calm, dependable, and showing little emotion or animation.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Emotionless, impassive, unemotional
3. **Sentences:**
    *  His **stolid** expression revealed nothing of his inner thoughts.
    *  The **stolid** guard stood motionless at his post.
4. **Opposite Words:** emotional, expressive
5. **GRE Synonyms:** impassive, phlegmatic

**32. temerity**
1. **Definition:** Excessive confidence or boldness; audacity.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Excessive boldness, reckless audacity
3. **Sentences:**
    *  He had the **temerity** to question the CEO's decision.
    *  Her **temerity** shocked everyone in the room.
4. **Opposite Words:** caution, timidity
5. **GRE Synonyms:** audacity, effrontery

**33. tenuous**
1. **Definition:** Very weak or slight.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Weak, flimsy, insubstantial
3. **Sentences:**
    *  The connection between the two events was **tenuous** at best.
    *  The evidence presented was too **tenuous** to convict him.
4. **Opposite Words:** strong, substantial
5. **GRE Synonyms:** flimsy, fragile

**34. verve**
1. **Definition:** Great energy and enthusiasm.
2. **Concise Meaning:** Energy, enthusiasm, and liveliness
3. **Sentences:**
    *  She performed with great **verve** and passion.
    *  His writing was full of **verve** and originality.
4. **Opposite Words:** apathy, lethargy
5. **GRE Synonyms:** vitality, exuberance
